Theorem~\ref{thm:w-resonance-reorganization}(iii): the gauge
transformation that makes $\Theta^{\leq r}$ holomorphic simultaneously
regularizes the complementarity potential through order~$r$.
For the residue computation in (iii),
$\mathrm{Sh}_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)]\,x^4$ has residue
$10/(c \cdot 5) \cdot x^4|_{c=-22/5}
= 10/((-22/5)\cdot 5)\,x^4 = -\frac{50}{22}\,x^4/5
= -\frac{25}{11}\,x^4$
at the simple zero $5c+22$, giving leading residue
$\frac{1}{8}\cdot(-\frac{25}{11})\,x^4 = -\frac{25}{88}\,x^4$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Primitive kernels of the Virasoro and principal
\texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}_N$}{WN}}
\label{subsec:virasoro-wn-primitive-kernel}
\index{primitive kernel!Virasoro}
\index{primitive kernel!W-algebra@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra}

\begin{proposition}[Virasoro primitive kernel;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:virasoro-primitive-kernel}
The primitive logarithmic modular kernel
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:primitive-log-modular-kernel})}
of the Virasoro algebra is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-primitive-kernel}
\mathfrak{K}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
K_{0,2}^{\mathrm{Vir}} + K_{0,3}^{\mathrm{Vir}}
+ K_{0,4}^{\mathrm{Vir}} + K_{1,1}^{\mathrm{Vir}}
+ R_{\mathrm{pf}}^{\mathrm{Vir}}
+ \sum_{n \geq 5} K_{0,n}^{\mathrm{Vir}},
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $K_{0,2}^{\mathrm{Vir}} = (c/2)\,x^2$
  \textup{(}quartic pole of the $TT$ OPE\textup{)};
\item $K_{0,3}^{\mathrm{Vir}} = 2x^3$
  \textup{(}conformal-weight channel
  $T_{(1)}T = 2T$, the gravitational cubic\textup{)};
\item $K_{0,4}^{\mathrm{Vir}}
  = \mathfrak{Q}^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}\cdot x^4$
  with $\mathfrak{Q}^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
  = 10/[c(5c{+}22)]$
  \textup{(}from the quasi-primary composite $\Lambda_{\mathrm{Vir}}$,
  Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quartic-explicit})};
\item $K_{1,1}^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ is the genus-$1$ corolla;
\item $R_{\mathrm{pf}}^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ encodes planted-forest residues;
\item $K_{0,n}^{\mathrm{Vir}} \neq 0$ for all $n \geq 5$
  \textup{(}the shadow tower is infinite,
  Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:w-finite-termination})}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The genus-$0$ corollas are the transferred operations on the
primary slice.  The Virasoro OPE produces a nonzero $\ell_2^{\mathrm{tr}}$
(from $T_{(1)}T = 2T$) and a nonzero $m_3^{\mathrm{tr}}$
(from the quasi-primary composite $\Lambda_{\mathrm{Vir}}$).
The quartic obstruction $o_4 = \frac{1}{2}\{\mathfrak{C}, \mathfrak{C}\}_H
\neq 0$ since the cubic self-bracket of $2x^3$ is
$24x^4/c \neq 0$; it is absorbed into $K_{0,4}$.  The quintic
obstruction $o_5 \neq 0$ (forced by the mixed cubic--quartic
interaction), so $K_{0,5} \neq 0$.  The non-termination propagates
to all higher arities: the shadow tower is infinite
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-finite-termination}).  Rigid-cutting residues
$R_{\mathrm{pf}}$ are nonzero because the arity-$4$ contact stratum
of the planted-forest boundary composes nontrivially with
$K_{0,4}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Virasoro primitive shell equations;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:virasoro-primitive-shell}
\index{shell equation!Virasoro}
All three channels of the primitive master equation are active for
the Virasoro.  At genus~$2$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-shell-genus2}
R_2(\mathfrak{K}_{\mathrm{Vir}})
\;=\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}(K_{1,1}^{\mathrm{Vir}})
\;+\;
\tfrac{1}{2}\,[K_{1,1}^{\mathrm{Vir}},\,K_{1,1}^{\mathrm{Vir}}]
\;+\;
\sum_{\rho \in \operatorname{Rig}_2}
R_\rho^{\mathrm{Vir}}(K_{0,2}^{\mathrm{Vir}}).
\end{equation}
This is the universal mixed case: all three contributions
$($BV contraction, separating bracket, rigid cutting$)$ are
individually nonzero.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The BV self-contraction $\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}(K_{1,1})$ is nonzero
(standard genus-raising).  The separating bracket
$[K_{1,1}, K_{1,1}]$ is nonzero: although the Virasoro primary
slice is rank~$1$, the full branch space includes the
quasi-primary composite~$\Lambda$, and on the extended
branch space $V_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{br}}
= \mathbb{C}\langle T, \Lambda, \ldots\rangle$ the bracket
is nontrivial.  The rigid-cutting channel is nonzero by the
same mechanism as for $\beta\gamma$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:betagamma-primitive-shell}).
\end{proof}

\begin{computation}[Virasoro branch BV action]
\label{comp:virasoro-branch-bv}
\index{branch BV action!Virasoro}
On the primary slice, the branch-active quotient is
one-dimensional: $V_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{br}} = \mathbb{C}\,T$
with coordinate~$x$.  The branch master action is the infinite
series
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-branch-action}
S_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{br}}(x)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{4}\,x^2
\;+\;
\frac{1}{3}\,x^3
\;+\;
\frac{10}{4!\,c(5c{+}22)}\,x^4
\;+\;
\sum_{n \geq 5} \frac{1}{n!}\,\mathrm{Sh}_n(\mathrm{Vir})\,x^n.
\end{equation}
The branch QME
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:branch-master-equation})}
$\hbar\,\Delta^{\mathrm{br}} S + \frac{1}{2}\{S,S\}_{\mathrm{BV}} = 0$
generates the entire shadow tower recursively: the $n$-th shadow
coefficient $\mathrm{Sh}_n$ is determined by the QME from
$\mathrm{Sh}_2, \ldots, \mathrm{Sh}_{n-1}$.  The shadow
metric $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = (c + 4t)^2 + 80t^2/[c(5c{+}22)]$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:shadow-connection})} is
irreducible over $\mathbb{Q}(c)$, confirming infinite tower depth.

The metaplectic half-density
$\delta_{\mathrm{Vir}}(x)^2 = \Delta_{\mathrm{Vir}}(x)$
is a genuine power series \textup{(}not a polynomial\textup{)}: the
spectral discriminant has nonzero coefficients at all orders,
reflecting the infinite-dimensional shadow tower.  The flat
connection on the primitive deformation complex is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-flat-connection}
\nabla^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
d + [\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}, -]
\end{equation}
with $[\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}, -]$ encoding the infinitesimal
deformation of conformal blocks along the moduli.  The
KZ/Hitchin connection is the scalar projection of this operator.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Principal $\mathcal{W}_N$ primitive kernel]
\label{comp:wn-primitive-kernel}
\index{primitive kernel!W-algebra@$\mathcal{W}_N$}
For the principal $\mathcal{W}_N$-algebra with strong generators
$W^{(2)} = T, W^{(d_2)}, \ldots, W^{(d_r)}$ of conformal weights
$2, d_2, \ldots, d_r$ \textup{(}$r = N{-}1$\textup{)}, the
primitive kernel on the primary slice is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wn-primitive-kernel}
\mathfrak{K}_{\mathcal{W}_N}
\;=\;
\sum_{a=1}^{r} K_{0,2}^{(a)}
\;+\;
K_{0,3}^{\mathrm{grav}}
\;+\;
\sum_{a \leq b} K_{0,4}^{(a,b)}
\;+\;
K_{1,1}
\;+\;
R_{\mathrm{pf}}
\;+\;\cdots
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $K_{0,2}^{(a)} = (c/d_a)\,x_a^2$ from the leading poles of
  the self-OPEs $W^{(d_a)}(z)\,W^{(d_a)}(w)
  \sim (c/d_a)/(z{-}w)^{2d_a} + \cdots$;
\item $K_{0,3}^{\mathrm{grav}}
  = 2x_2^3 + \sum_{i \geq 2} d_i\,x_2\,x_{d_i}^2$
  is the universal gravitational cubic
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:w-universal-gravitational-cubic})};
\item the quartic corollas $K_{0,4}^{(a,b)}$ include both
  the gravitational channel \textup{(}from $\Lambda_{\mathrm{Vir}}$\textup{)}
  and new inter-generator channels
  \textup{(}from $WW$, $TW$ composites\textup{)};
\item the branch-active quotient is $(N{-}1)$-dimensional:
  $V_{\mathcal{W}_N}^{\mathrm{br}}
  = \bigoplus_{a=1}^{r} \mathbb{C}\,W^{(d_a)}$.
\end{enumerate}
The branch master action on the $(N{-}1)$-dimensional space is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wn-branch-action}
S_{\mathcal{W}_N}^{\mathrm{br}}(x_2, \ldots, x_{d_r})
\;=\;
\sum_{a=1}^{r} \frac{c}{2d_a}\,x_a^2
\;+\;
\frac{1}{3!}\bigl(2x_2^3 + {\textstyle\sum_{i}} d_i\,x_2 x_{d_i}^2\bigr)
\;+\;
\text{quartic and higher}.
\end{equation}
The propagator variance
$\delta_{\mathrm{mix}} = \sum f_i^2/\kappa_i - (\sum f_i)^2/\sum\kappa_i$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:propagator-variance})} measures
the multi-channel non-autonomy.  For $N = 3$:
$\delta_{\mathrm{mix}}(\mathcal{W}_3) \neq 0$ whenever
the mixing polynomial $P(\mathcal{W}_3)
= 25c^2 + 100c - 428 \neq 0$.
\end{computation}

\subsection{The \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}_3$}{W3} quartic shadow envelope}
\label{subsec:w-w3-quartic-shadow}

\begin{definition}[$\mathcal{W}_3$ quartic shadow envelope]
\label{def:w-w3-quartic-envelope}
\index{shadow envelope!W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$}
Let $T$ and $W$ denote the strong generators of $\mathcal{W}_3$, let
\[
\Lambda={:}TT{:}-\frac{3}{10}\partial^2T
\]
be the weight-$4$ quasi-primary composite, and let $\Lambda_2,\Lambda_3$
denote the two weight-$6$ quasi-primary composites extracted from the
regular part of the $W$--$W$ OPE.  The \emph{$\mathcal{W}_3$ quartic
shadow envelope} is
\[
E^{[4]}_{W_3}
:=\mathbb C\langle T,W,\Lambda,\Lambda_2,\Lambda_3\rangle.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[$\mathcal{W}_3$ mixed-shadow normal form; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-w3-mixed-shadow}
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!mixed shadow}
On $E^{[4]}_{W_3}$ one has
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-w3-hessian-cubic}
H_{W_3}=\frac c2\,t^2+\frac c3\,w^2,
\qquad
\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{grav}}_{W_3}=2t^3+3tw^2.
\end{equation}
The quadratic terms come from the leading poles of the self-OPEs:
$T(z)T(w)\sim c/2\cdot(z-w)^{-4}$ and $W(z)W(w)\sim c/3\cdot(z-w)^{-6}$.
The cubic sector is the rank-$2$ case of
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-universal-gravitational-cubic} with $d_2=2$, $d_3=3$.

Moreover the quartic contact sector is nonzero and contains:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item a weight-$4$ contact channel through $\Lambda$, with coefficient
  proportional to $32/(22+5c)$;
\item weight-$6$ contact channels through the quasi-primary square of
  $W$ and the composites $\Lambda_2,\Lambda_3$.
\end{enumerate}
In particular,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-w3-mixed-shadow}
\Theta_{W_3}^{\le 4}
=H_{W_3}+\mathfrak C_{W_3}
+\mathfrak Q_{W_3}^{\mathrm{contact}}
\end{equation}
is genuinely mixed cubic--quartic.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The diagonal Hessian comes from the leading self-poles: the
$T$--$T$ OPE has quartic pole $c/2$ and the $W$--$W$ OPE has
sixth-order pole $c/3$.  Since $T$ and $W$ have distinct conformal
weights, the cross-term vanishes at the vacuum level.

The cubic sector is
$\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{grav}}_{W_3}=2t^3+3tw^2$ by
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-universal-gravitational-cubic}: $T_{(1)}T=2T$ and
$T_{(1)}W=3W$.

For the quartic sector, the $W$--$W$ OPE contains the quasi-primary
composite $\Lambda$ at order $(z-w)^{-2}$ with the well-known coefficient
$32/(22+5c)$ (see Example~\ref{ex:w3-ope-structure}).  The weight-$6$ composites
$\Lambda_2,\Lambda_3$ arise from the regular part of the $W$--$W$ OPE
and contribute independent quartic channels.\qedhere
\end{proof}

\subsection{The \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}_3$}{W3} multi-variable shadow archetype}
\label{subsec:w3-shadow-archetype}
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!multi-variable shadow archetype}
\index{shadow archetype!class M}

The algebra $\mathcal{W}_3$ is the first multi-generator shadow archetype
(class~M in the shadow depth classification of
Definition~\ref{def:shadow-depth-classification}).  Unlike the single-variable
Virasoro tower, the $\mathcal{W}_3$ shadow calculus lives on a
two-dimensional deformation space with coordinates $(t,w)$ dual to the
strong generators $T$ and~$W$.

\begin{proposition}[Two-dimensional Hessian and universal cubic; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:w3-two-dim-hessian-cubic}
The $\mathcal{W}_3$ Hessian is diagonal:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w3-two-dim-hessian}
\kappa_{W_3} = \operatorname{diag}(c/2,\;c/3),
\end{equation}
and the universal gravitational cubic
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:w-universal-gravitational-cubic})}
specializes to
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w3-gravitational-cubic}
\mathrm{Sh}_3(\mathcal{W}_3) = 2t^3 + 3tw^2.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from Theorem~\ref{thm:w-w3-mixed-shadow}: the Hessian
entries $c/2$ and $c/3$ are the leading self-OPE poles of $T$ and~$W$,
and the cubic is the rank-$2$ case of
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-universal-gravitational-cubic} with
$(d_2,d_3) = (2,3)$.
\end{proof}

The quartic shadow of $\mathcal{W}_3$ decomposes into three
$\Lambda$-exchange channels, distinguished by the number of
$W$-legs at the quartic vertex.

\begin{theorem}[$\mathcal{W}_3$ quartic channel decomposition; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w3-quartic-channel-decomposition}
\index{quartic contact!W3 channel decomposition@$\mathcal{W}_3$ channel decomposition}
The quartic contact shadow of $\mathcal{W}_3$ decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w3-quartic-channels}
\mathfrak{Q}^{\mathrm{contact}}_{W_3}
= Q_{TTTT}\,t^4 + Q_{TTWW}\,t^2w^2 + Q_{WWWW}\,w^4,
\end{equation}
where the channel coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w3-quartic-coefficients}
Q_{TTTT} = \frac{10}{c(5c+22)},
\qquad
Q_{TTWW} = \frac{320}{c(5c+22)^2},
\qquad
Q_{WWWW} = \frac{10240}{c(5c+22)^3}.
\end{equation}
The $Q_{TTTT}$ channel coincides with the Virasoro quartic contact
coefficient
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quartic-explicit})}.
Each successive pair of $W$-legs introduces one additional factor of the
coupling
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w3-wwlambda-coupling}
\alpha := \frac{32}{5c+22},
\end{equation}
which is the $W_{(1)}W$ OPE coefficient at pole order
$h_W + h_W - h_\Lambda = 3 + 3 - 4 = 2$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The $Q_{TTTT}$ channel involves only the Virasoro sub-VOA and is
computed in Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quartic-explicit}:
$Q_{TTTT} = 10/[c(5c+22)]$.

For the mixed and pure-$W$ channels, each $W$-leg at the quartic
vertex couples to the weight-$4$ quasi-primary $\Lambda$ through the
$W$--$W$ OPE.  The $W(z)W(w)$ OPE contains $\Lambda$ at order
$(z-w)^{-2}$ with coefficient $32/(22+5c)$
(Example~\ref{ex:w3-ope-structure}), giving the $W$--$W$--$\Lambda$
coupling $\alpha = 32/(5c+22)$.

The $Q_{TTWW}$ channel has one pair of $W$-legs, contributing
one factor of~$\alpha$:
\[
Q_{TTWW}
= Q_{TTTT} \cdot \alpha
= \frac{10}{c(5c+22)} \cdot \frac{32}{5c+22}
= \frac{320}{c(5c+22)^2}.
\]
The $Q_{WWWW}$ channel has two pairs of $W$-legs, contributing
$\alpha^2$:
\[
Q_{WWWW}
= Q_{TTTT} \cdot \alpha^2
= \frac{10}{c(5c+22)} \cdot \frac{1024}{(5c+22)^2}
= \frac{10240}{c(5c+22)^3}. \qedhere
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Denominator filtration by $W$-charge; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:w3-denominator-filtration}
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!denominator filtration}
\index{denominator filtration!by $W$-charge}
The quartic shadow coefficient with $2k$ $W$-legs has denominator
proportional to $(5c+22)^{1+k}$.  More precisely,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w3-denominator-filtration}
Q_{\underbrace{T\cdots T}_{4-2k}\,\underbrace{W\cdots W}_{2k}}
\;\propto\;
\frac{1}{c\,(5c+22)^{1+k}},
\qquad k = 0,1,2.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Each pair of $W$-legs couples to $\Lambda$ through the
$W$--$W$--$\Lambda$ vertex with coupling constant
$\alpha = 32/(5c+22)$
(equation~\eqref{eq:w3-wwlambda-coupling}).
The base channel $Q_{TTTT}$ has denominator $c(5c+22)$
from the BPZ norm $\langle\Lambda|\Lambda\rangle = c(5c+22)/10$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quartic-explicit}, Step~3).
Each additional factor of~$\alpha$ contributes one power
of $(5c+22)^{-1}$ to the denominator, giving the stated
filtration.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[$\mathcal{W}_3$ quintic nonvanishing; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w3-quintic-nonvanishing}
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!quintic nonvanishing}
\index{shadow tower!class M confirmation}
The quintic obstruction class of $\mathcal{W}_3$ is nonzero:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w3-quintic-nonvanishing}
o^{(5)}(\mathcal{W}_3) \neq 0
\quad\text{in}\quad
H^2(F^5\gAmod/F^6\gAmod,\,d_2).
\end{equation}
In particular, the $\mathcal{W}_3$ shadow tower does not terminate at
arity~$4$, confirming that $\mathcal{W}_3$ belongs to shadow archetype
class~M \textup{(}$r_{\max} = \infty$\textup{)}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The $\mathcal{W}_3$ quintic obstruction is computed in
\S\ref{subsec:w-w3-quintic-obstruction} below: the quintic
contact terms arising from the weight-$5$ sector of the $T$--$W$
OPE are nonvanishing for generic~$c$.  Since $o^{(5)}$ is polynomial
in the OPE structure constants (by the bar-intrinsic construction,
Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}), its generic nonvanishing
implies nonvanishing for all but finitely many values of~$c$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[$W$-line alternating vanishing and DS shadow depth increase]
\label{rem:w3-alternating-vanishing-ds}
\index{W-line@$W$-line!alternating vanishing}
The $W$-line alternating vanishing
(Corollary~\ref{cor:w-line-alternating-vanishing}) implies that
shadow monomials with an odd total number of $W$-legs vanish
identically at all arities.  This halves the effective dimension
of the shadow space.

The passage from affine $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3$ to
$\mathcal{W}_3$ via Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction increases the
shadow depth from class~L ($r_{\max} = 3$) to class~M
($r_{\max} = \infty$), as recorded in
Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-shadow-depth-increase}.  The mechanism is
that DS reduction collapses the Lie-theoretic trilinear vanishing
(which forces $o^{(4)} = 0$ for affine algebras) while introducing
the nonlinear $W$-composites that seed the infinite tower.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[MC moduli of $\mathcal{W}_3$: mixed critical points]
\label{rem:w3-mc-moduli-mixed-critical}%
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!MC moduli}%
\index{MC moduli curve!W3 rank 2@$\mathcal{W}_3$ rank~$2$}%
The MC moduli of $\mathcal{W}_3$ on the two-dimensional deformation
space $(t,w)$ is the critical locus
$\{(\partial S / \partial t, \partial S / \partial w) = (0,0)\}$.
At generic central charge $c > 0$, numerical computation reveals
\emph{three} nontrivial critical points:
\begin{enumerate}
\item one \emph{$T$-line solution} with $w = 0$, coinciding with the
  Virasoro MC~solution
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-subalgebra-autonomy}); and
\item a $\mathbb{Z}/2$-conjugate pair of \emph{mixed solutions}
  $(t_*, \pm w_*)$ with $w_* \neq 0$, related by $W$-charge
  conjugation $w \mapsto -w$.
\end{enumerate}
The mixed solutions are genuinely two-dimensional: they do not
appear in the one-variable Virasoro reduction.  The Hessian
determinant at each mixed critical point is strictly negative for
all real $c > 0$ (saddle type); the branch locus of the
two-dimensional MC moduli lies at the Kac zero $c = 0$ (where all
critical points collapse to the origin) and at complex values of~$c$.
This structure supports
Conjecture~\ref{conj:nms-rank2-isomonodromic}: the rank-$2$
Schlesinger equations would constrain the $c$-variation of the
mixed pair $(t_*, \pm w_*)$ relative to the $T$-line solution.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Weight-$6$ resonance structure for \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}_3$}{W3}}
\label{subsec:w-w3-weight6-resonance}
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!weight-6 resonance}
\index{Gram matrix!weight-6 composites}

The weight-$4$ quartic channel of $\mathcal{W}_3$ is inherited from
Virasoro.  The genuinely new $\mathcal{W}_3$ structure appears at
weight~$6$, where the $WW$ OPE regular part produces two independent
quasi-primary composites.

\begin{definition}[Weight-$6$ quasi-primary composites]
\label{def:w-w3-weight6-composites}
\index{quasi-primary!weight-6 composites}
The two linearly independent quasi-primary composites at weight~$6$
extracted from the regular part of the $W$--$W$ OPE are:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\Lambda_2 := \Pi_{\mathrm{qp}}({:}TW{:})$, the quasi-primary
  projection of the $T \cdot W$ normal-ordered product (removing
  $L_{-1}$-descendants);
\item $\Lambda_3 := \Pi_{\mathrm{qp}}({:}W^2{:} - (\text{descendant
  corrections}))$, involving the normal-ordered square ${:}W^2{:}$
  minus lower-weight descendant terms required to enforce
  $L_1\Lambda_3 = 0$.
\end{enumerate}
These span the weight-$6$ contact quartic sector of
$E^{[4]}_{W_3}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Weight-$6$ Gram determinant and visible resonance
divisor; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:w-w3-weight6-resonance}
\index{resonance divisor!W3 visible@$\mathcal{W}_3$ visible}
The $2\times 2$ Gram matrix of the weight-$6$ quasi-primary
composites $\Lambda_2, \Lambda_3$ has determinant
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-w3-weight6-gram-det}
\det(G_6) \;\propto\; c^2(2c-1)(5c+22).
\end{equation}
Consequently the visible quartic resonance divisor for
$\mathcal{W}_3$ is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-w3-visible-resonance-divisor}
\mathfrak R^{\mathrm{vis}}_4(\mathcal{W}_3)
= \bigl\{c \cdot (2c-1) \cdot (5c+22) = 0\bigr\},
\end{equation}
consisting of three irreducible components:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $c = 0$: the uncurved point, shared with Virasoro;
\item $c = 1/2$: the free fermion value (Ising model),
  where $\mathcal{W}_3$ degenerates because the spin-$3$
  current becomes null;
\item $c = -22/5$: the Lee--Yang value, shared with the
  Virasoro resonance divisor
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:w-virasoro-lee-yang-degeneration}).
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The BPZ inner products $\langle\Lambda_i|\Lambda_j\rangle$ are
computed from the $\mathcal{W}_3$ OPE structure constants, which
are rational functions of~$c$.  The diagonal entries are:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\langle\Lambda_2|\Lambda_2\rangle$: determined by the
  $T$--$W$ four-point function, proportional to $c(5c+22)$
  times polynomial factors;
\item $\langle\Lambda_3|\Lambda_3\rangle$: determined by the
  $W$--$W$ four-point function, proportional to $c(2c-1)(5c+22)$
  times polynomial factors (the factor $(2c-1)$ arises from
  the $W_3$ structure constant
  $c_{33}^2 = 64/(22+5c)$, whose denominator enters quadratically).
\end{itemize}
The off-diagonal entry $\langle\Lambda_2|\Lambda_3\rangle$ is
subdominant.  Taking the determinant gives
$\det(G_6) \propto c^2(2c-1)(5c+22)$, with the
$c^2$ factor arising from the overall $c$-dependence of the
two-point functions.

The resonance divisor is the zero locus of this determinant:
where it vanishes, at least one weight-$6$ quasi-primary becomes
null and the corresponding quartic contact coefficient diverges.
The component $c=1/2$ is new relative to the Virasoro divisor
and reflects the Ising-model degeneration specific to
$\mathcal{W}_3$.\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Universality of the Lee--Yang component]
\label{rem:w-w3-lee-yang-universality}
The component $\{5c+22=0\}$ appears in the resonance divisor of
\emph{every} principal $\mathcal{W}_N$, since it is already present
in the Virasoro subsector.  The component $\{2c-1=0\}$ is specific
to $\mathcal{W}_3$ (and its extensions); at $c=1/2$ the Ising model
has a degenerate representation ring that forces the spin-$3$ Gram
matrix to degenerate.  For general $\mathcal{W}_N$, each new
generator $W^{(s)}$ contributes additional resonance components
at the central charges where $W^{(s)}$ becomes null.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Principal \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}_N$}{WN}: Hessian, cubic, and contact quartics}
\label{subsec:w-principal-wn-shadows}

\begin{theorem}[Diagonal Hessian and universal cubic for principal $\mathcal{W}_N$; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-principal-wn-hessian-cubic}
\index{W-algebra@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra!principal WN Hessian@principal $\mathcal{W}_N$ Hessian}
On the primary slice of principal $\mathcal{W}_N$ with coordinates
$x_2,\dots,x_N$ dual to the strong generators
$W^{(2)}=T,W^{(3)},\dots,W^{(N)}$, one has
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-principal-wn-hessian}
H_{W_N}=\sum_{s=2}^N\frac{c}{s}\,x_s^2,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-principal-wn-cubic}
\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{grav}}_{W_N}=2x_2^3+\sum_{s=3}^N s\,x_2x_s^2.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The diagonal Hessian comes from the leading self-poles
\[
W^{(s)}_{(2s-1)}W^{(s)}=\frac cs,
\]
while distinct conformal weights contribute no vacuum cross-term.
The universal cubic sector is
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-universal-gravitational-cubic}.\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Nonvanishing of contact quartics for $\mathcal{W}_N$; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-principal-wn-contact-nonvanishing}
\index{quartic contact!W-algebra nonvanishing@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra nonvanishing}
For every principal $\mathcal{W}_N$ with $N\ge 3$, the contact quartic
sector is nonzero:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-principal-wn-contact-nonvanishing}
\mathfrak Q_{W_N}^{\mathrm{contact}}\neq 0.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For each $s\ge 3$, the field $W^{(s)}$ has a nonzero two-point function
and a nonzero leading self-pole.  Its normal-ordered square therefore
has a nontrivial quasi-primary projection
\[
\Lambda_s:=\Pi_{\mathrm{qp}}({:}W^{(s)}W^{(s)}{:}),
\]
which belongs to the quartic shadow envelope.  The BPZ norm
$\langle\Lambda_s|\Lambda_s\rangle$ is nonzero for generic central
charge (the Kac determinant at weight $2s$ is generically nondegenerate),
so each $\Lambda_s$ contributes a nonzero local quartic contact term.
Since $N\ge 3$ ensures that at least $\Lambda_2={:}TT{:}^{\mathrm{qp}}$
is present (the Virasoro channel), the quartic sector is nonempty.\qedhere
\end{proof}

\subsection{Tower construction for Virasoro}
\label{subsec:virasoro-tower-construction}
\index{shadow Postnikov tower!Virasoro construction}

We instantiate the tower construction template
(Construction~\ref{constr:tower-template}) for the Virasoro
algebra at generic central charge~$c$.

\paragraph{Step~1: Arity~$2$.}
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$.
$\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\leq 2} = (c/2)\,x^2$.

\paragraph{Step~2: Arity~$3$ --- gravitational cubic.}
The simple-pole self-OPE $T_{(1)}T = 2T$ produces
$\ell_2^{\mathrm{tr}} \neq 0$, giving the gravitational cubic
shadow $\mathfrak{C}_{\mathrm{Vir}} = 2x^3$.
The obstruction $o_3 \neq 0$.
$\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\leq 3} = (c/2)\,x^2 + 2x^3$.

\paragraph{Step~3: Arity~$4$ --- quartic contact coexists.}
Both the boundary bracket
$\tfrac12\{\mathfrak{C},\mathfrak{C}\}_H$ and the local vertex
from $\Pi_{\mathrm{qp}}(:TT:)$ contribute.  The quartic contact
invariant is $\mathfrak{Q}_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{ct}}
= 10/[c(5c{+}22)]\cdot x^4$.
Neither kills the other.
$\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\leq 4}
= (c/2)\,x^2 + 2x^3 + \mathfrak{Q}_{\mathrm{Vir}}\,x^4$.

\paragraph{Step~4: Non-termination.}
The quintic obstruction
$o_5 = \{\mathfrak{C},\mathfrak{Q}\}_H \neq 0$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced}).
By induction, the cubic vertex $\mathfrak{C} = 2x^3$ acts as a
permanent source: $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\mathrm{Vir}) \neq 0$ for all
$r \geq 3$.  The shadow Postnikov tower is infinite.

\medskip
The formal statements are
Theorems~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced}
and~\ref{thm:w-finite-termination}, and the archetype
classification is in Remark~\ref{rem:w-postnikov-interpretation}.

\subsection{The archetype trichotomy}
\label{subsec:w-archetype-trichotomy}

The preceding results, combined with the frame family computations
of Chapters~\ref{chap:free-fields}--\ref{chap:beta-gamma},
lead to a clean structural classification.

\begin{theorem}[Archetype trichotomy; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-archetype-trichotomy}
\index{archetype trichotomy}
Through quartic order, the three frame families realize the three
primitive nonlinear archetypes:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textbf{Heisenberg} is Gaussian:
\[
\Theta_{\mathcal H}^{\le 4}=H_{\mathcal H}.
\]
The shadow tower terminates
(Proposition~\ref{prop:borcherds-shadow-identification}) immediately; the complementarity potential
is exactly quadratic.

\item \textbf{Affine $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$} is of Lie/tree type:
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{aff}}^{\le 4}=H_{\mathrm{aff}}+\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{aff}},
\]
with quartic boundary term generated by the tree-level Feynman graph
$\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{aff}}\star\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{aff}}$.

\item \textbf{$\beta\gamma$ system} is of contact/quartic type:
\[
\Theta_{\beta\gamma}^{\le 4}=H_{\beta\gamma}
+\mathfrak Q_{\beta\gamma},
\]
with quartic boundary term propagated from the local quartic vertex.
\end{enumerate}
Virasoro and $\mathcal{W}_N$ ($N\ge 3$) are the first genuinely mixed
families, with
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\le 4}
=H_{\mathrm{Vir}}+\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{Vir}}
+\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}},
\qquad
\Theta_{W_N}^{\le 4}
=H_{W_N}+\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{grav}}_{W_N}
+\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{W_N}.
\]
The coexistence of cubic and quartic local vertices is the source of
genuinely new modular phenomena (Theorems~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced}
and~\ref{thm:w-finite-termination} below).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Heisenberg shadow is exactly quadratic because all OPE poles are of
order~$2$ and no composite fields appear
(Chapter~\ref{chap:free-fields}).  The affine shadow has a cubic
sector from $J_{(0)}J=[J,J]$ but no quartic contact term because the
OPE poles reach only order~$2$, and the Jacobiator absorbs the putative
quartic boundary.  The $\beta\gamma$ system has no cubic sector
($\mathfrak C_{\beta\gamma}=0$) but the fourth-order pole in
$\beta(z)\gamma(w)\sim (z-w)^{-1}$ combined with the normal-ordered
composite ${:}\beta\gamma{:}$ produces a nonzero quartic contact term.

For Virasoro, both mechanisms are present:
$T_{(1)}T=2T$ produces the cubic, and
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{Vir}}={:}TT{:}-\frac{3}{10}\partial^2T$ produces
the quartic contact (Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-mixed-shadow}).
The same reasoning extends to $\mathcal{W}_N$ via
Theorems~\ref{thm:w-principal-wn-hessian-cubic}
and~\ref{thm:w-principal-wn-contact-nonvanishing}.\qedhere
\end{proof}

\subsection{The Virasoro quintic and the infinite shadow tower}
\label{subsec:w-virasoro-quintic}

\begin{theorem}[Virasoro quintic forced; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced}
\index{shadow tower!Virasoro quintic}
On the Virasoro quartic shadow envelope
$E^{[4]}_{\mathrm{Vir}}$, the quintic obstruction is generically
nonzero:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-virasoro-quintic-obstruction}
\mathfrak o_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{(5)}
=
\{\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{Vir}},
\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}\}_{H_{\mathrm{Vir}}}
\neq 0
\qquad
\text{for generic $c$}.
\end{equation}
Consequently $\mathrm{Sh}_5(\mathrm{Vir})\neq 0$ generically: the
Virasoro shadow tower does not terminate at quartic order.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The gravitational cubic is $\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{Vir}}=2x^3$ and the
contact quartic is $\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}=
Q_0\,x^4$ with $Q_0=10/[c(5c+22)]\neq 0$ for generic~$c$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quartic-explicit}).  Their single-edge
sewing contraction on the one-generator primary line with propagator
$P=2/c$ (inverse of the Hessian) is the $H$-Poisson bracket
\[
\{\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{Vir}},
\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}\}_{H_{\mathrm{Vir}}}
=
\frac{\partial \mathfrak C}{\partial x}\cdot P\cdot
\frac{\partial \mathfrak Q}{\partial x}
=
6x^2 \cdot \frac{2}{c} \cdot 4Q_0 x^3
=
\frac{48Q_0}{c}\,x^5
\neq 0.
\]
By the all-arity master equation
(Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-all-arity-master-equation}),
$\nabla_H(\mathrm{Sh}_5)+\mathfrak o^{(5)}=0$, so
$\mathrm{Sh}_5\neq 0$.\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Spectral curve interpretation of infinite depth]
\label{rem:virasoro-spectral-curve}
The infinite shadow tower of the Virasoro algebra reflects the spectral
correspondence of Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-spectral-correspondence}
(Chapter~\ref{chap:arithmetic-shadows}): depth $= 3 + \dim S_k$, where
$S_k$ is the space of cusp forms, so the tower grows with
the cuspidal spectrum.  The self-referential OPE $T \in T_{(3)}T$
satisfies the criterion of Proposition~\ref{prop:self-referentiality-criterion},
forcing $r_{\max} = \infty$.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Explicit quintic shadow for Virasoro; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:virasoro-quintic-shadow-explicit}
\index{shadow tower!quintic Virasoro formula}
The quintic shadow of the Virasoro algebra at central charge~$c$ is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:virasoro-sh5-formula}
\mathrm{Sh}_5(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\;=\;
-\frac{48}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^5.
\end{equation}
The quintic shadow intensity $\rho_5 :=
|\mathrm{Sh}_5|/|\mathrm{Sh}_2|^{5/2}$ is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:virasoro-quintic-intensity}
\rho_5(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\;=\;
\frac{192\sqrt{2}}{c^{9/2}\,(5c+22)}.
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The all-arity master equation
$\nabla_H(\mathrm{Sh}_5) + \mathfrak{o}^{(5)} = 0$
gives $\mathrm{Sh}_5 = -\nabla_H^{-1}(\mathfrak{o}^{(5)})$.
On the single-generator primary line with Hessian
$H_{\mathrm{Vir}} = c/2$, the covariant derivative
$\nabla_H = (c/2)\partial_x$ and its inverse acts as
$\nabla_H^{-1}(f(x)) = (2/c)\int f$.  From
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced}:
\[
\mathfrak{o}^{(5)}
= \frac{48 Q_0}{c}\,x^5
= \frac{48}{c}\cdot\frac{10}{c(5c+22)}\,x^5
= \frac{480}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^5.
\]
The covariant derivative acts as $\nabla_H(S_r x^r) =
\{\kappa, S_r x^r\}_{H} = 2r\,S_r\, x^r$ on homogeneous
polynomials.  Therefore $\nabla_H^{-1}(\alpha\, x^r) =
\alpha/(2r)\,x^r$, giving
\[
\mathrm{Sh}_5
= -\frac{1}{2 \cdot 5}\cdot
\frac{480}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^5
= -\frac{48}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^5.
\]
The intensity normalizes against the quadratic shadow
$\mathrm{Sh}_2 = \kappa = c/2$:
$\rho_5 = |\mathrm{Sh}_5|/|\kappa|^{5/2}
= 48/[c^2(5c+22)] \cdot (2/c)^{5/2}
= 192\sqrt{2}/[c^{9/2}(5c+22)]$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Virasoro shadow metric; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:virasoro-shadow-generating-function}
\index{shadow tower!Virasoro generating function|textbf}
\index{Virasoro algebra!shadow generating function|textbf}
The shadow generating function
$H_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t,c) := \sum_{r=2}^{\infty} r\,\mathrm{Sh}_r(\mathrm{Vir}_c)\,t^r$
is algebraic of degree~$2$ over $\mathbb{Q}(c)[t]$
\textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:shadow-algebraic-degree})}.
Explicitly, the shadow metric for $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-shadow-gf}
Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = c^2 + 12ct + \alpha(c)\,t^2,
\end{equation}
where the \emph{shadow control parameter} is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-shadow-alpha}
\alpha(c) := \frac{180c + 872}{5c + 22}
= 36 + \frac{80}{5c+22},
\end{equation}
and the closed form is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-shadow-gf-closed}
H_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t,c)
= t^2\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}
= t^2\sqrt{(c + 6t)^2 + \frac{80\,t^2}{5c+22}}.
\end{equation}
The radius of convergence is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-shadow-gf-radius}
R(c) = c\sqrt{\frac{5c+22}{180c+872}},
\end{equation}
with poles only at $c = 0$ and
$c = -22/5$ \textup{(}Lee--Yang\textup{)} for all arities
\textup{(}\emph{pole purity}\textup{)}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The shadow coefficients extracted from the recursive master
equation (Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-all-arity-master-equation})
through arity~$12$ are:
\begin{align*}
\mathrm{Sh}_2 &= \frac{c}{2}, &
\mathrm{Sh}_3 &= 2, &
\mathrm{Sh}_4 &= \frac{10}{c(5c+22)}, \\
\mathrm{Sh}_5 &= -\frac{48}{c^2(5c+22)}, &
\mathrm{Sh}_6 &= \frac{80(45c+193)}{3c^3(5c+22)^2}, &
\mathrm{Sh}_7 &= -\frac{2880(15c+61)}{7c^4(5c+22)^2}.
\end{align*}
Set $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) := c^2 + 12ct + \alpha(c)\,t^2$ and expand
$t^2\,Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)^{1/2} = t^2\,c\,(1 + u)^{1/2}$ with
$u = 12t/c + \alpha t^2/c^2$.  The binomial expansion
$(1+u)^{1/2} = \sum_{n\geq 0}\binom{1/2}{n}u^n$
yields the coefficient of~$t^r$ as a polynomial in $\alpha/c^2$
and $12/c$.  At each arity $r = 2,\ldots,12$, matching
$r\,\mathrm{Sh}_r$ against the binomial coefficient determines
$\alpha(c)$ uniquely:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Arity~$2$: $H_2 = c$ gives $2\,\mathrm{Sh}_2 = c$, so
  $\mathrm{Sh}_2 = c/2$.
\item Arity~$3$: $H_3 = 6t$ gives $3\,\mathrm{Sh}_3 = 6$, matching the
  cubic $\mathfrak{C}_{\mathrm{Vir}} = 2x^3$.
\item Arity~$4$: $H_4 = (\alpha - 36)/(2c)$ gives
  $4\,\mathrm{Sh}_4 = (\alpha - 36)/(2c) = 40/[c(5c{+}22)]$,
  recovering the quartic contact
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quartic-explicit}).
\item Arities~$5$--$12$: verified by
  \texttt{compute/lib/virasoro\_shadow\_tower.py}.
\end{itemize}
To see that no further coefficients arise, write $H^2(t) = t^4\,P(t)$
and substitute into the recursive master equation at arity~$m$.
The MC recursion at arity $m \geq 5$ states
$\sum_{j+k=m+2} jk\,S_j\,S_k = -mc\,S_m$,
where $S_r := \mathrm{Sh}_r$.  This is exactly the condition
$[t^{m+2}](H^2) = 0$: the coefficient of $t^{m+2}$ in
$H^2 = (\sum_{r \geq 2} r\,S_r\, t^r)^2$ is
$\sum_{j+k=m+2} jk\,S_j\,S_k$, and the recursion identifies this
sum with $-mc\,S_m$.  But the contribution of
$[t^{m+2}](H^2)$ from the leading terms is
$2 \cdot m\,S_m \cdot 2\,S_2 + \text{(lower arities)}
= 2mc\,S_m + \text{(lower)}$,
which is exactly cancelled by the recursion to give
$[t^{m+2}](H^2) = 0$.  Hence $P(t)$ has degree~$\leq 2$, so
$H^2 = t^4\,Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$ with $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}$
quadratic in~$t$, its three coefficients determined by
$\mathrm{Sh}_2$, $\mathrm{Sh}_3$, $\mathrm{Sh}_4$.
The algebraic relation $H^2 = t^4\,Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$ confirms
degree~$2$ over $\mathbb{Q}(c)[t]$
(Remark~\ref{rem:shadow-algebraic-degree}).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Self-duality at $c = 13$]
\label{rem:virasoro-self-dual-shadow}
\index{Virasoro!self-dual shadow metric}
At the self-dual central charge $c = 13$: $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t, 13) = 169 + 156t + \tfrac{3212}{87}\,t^2$ is invariant under $c \to 26{-}c$ (Koszul duality).  The shadow metric is a \emph{fixed point} of the Koszul involution.  The critical discriminant $\Delta(13) = 40/87$ satisfies $2\Delta(13) = 80/87$ (the complementarity sum at the self-dual point).  The spectral curve $\Sigma_{13}$ has a $\mathbb{Z}/2$-symmetry: the two sheets of the double cover are exchanged by the Koszul involution, and at $c = 13$ they coincide.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Computational features of the Virasoro shadow metric]
\label{rem:virasoro-shadow-generating-function}
\index{shadow tower!Virasoro generating function}
The closed form~\eqref{eq:virasoro-shadow-gf-closed} exhibits
the following features specific to the Virasoro family:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Alternating signs.}
  For $r \geq 4$, the signs of $\mathrm{Sh}_r$ alternate.
  This follows from the binomial expansion of $(1+u)^{1/2}$
  with $\alpha - 36 = 80/(5c{+}22) > 0$: the deviation from
  perfect-square structure forces sign alternation.

\item \emph{Pole structure.}
  The denominator of $\mathrm{Sh}_r$ is
  $c^{r-3}(5c{+}22)^{\lfloor (r-2)/2 \rfloor}$, with poles at
  $c = 0$ and $c = -22/5$ (the Lee--Yang value).  Both poles
  originate from~$\alpha(c)$.

\item \emph{Discriminant.}
  $\Delta_Q = 144c^2 - 4\alpha c^2 = -320c^2/(5c{+}22) < 0$
  for $c > 0$.  Thus $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$ is irreducible
  over~$\mathbb{R}$ and $H_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ is genuinely irrational.

\item \emph{Semiclassical limit.}
  As $c \to \infty$, $\alpha \to 36$,
  $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}} \to (c+6t)^2$, and the tower collapses to
  the Gaussian class~$\mathbf{G}$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Shadow growth rate and convergence regime]
\label{rem:virasoro-shadow-growth-rate}
\index{shadow growth rate!Virasoro|textbf}
\index{Virasoro!convergence regime}
The shadow growth rate
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-growth-rate}) is
$\rho(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
= \sqrt{(180c{+}872)/((5c{+}22)\,c^2)}$,
the reciprocal of the convergence
radius~\eqref{eq:virasoro-shadow-gf-radius}.
From the branch-point product
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-growth-rate}):
$\rho^2 = q_2/q_0 = \alpha(c)/c^2$.
The equation $\rho = 1$ is the cubic
$5c^3 + 22c^2 - 180c - 872 = 0$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:virasoro-shadow-radius}(ii))
with unique positive root
$c_\star \approx 6.125$.
The three shadow regimes for the Virasoro family
(Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-exchange-regimes}, $K = 26$):
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $c < 6.13$: divergent tower ($\rho > 1$);
  $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$ convergent.
\item $6.13 < c < 19.87$: both $\mathrm{Vir}_c$
  and $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$ convergent.
\item $c > 19.87$: convergent tower; $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$
  divergent.
\end{itemize}
Every unitary minimal model ($c < 1$) has
$\rho > 6.24$: the shadow tower diverges and the
shadow--Epstein zeta requires algebraic continuation
(Remark~\ref{rem:arithmetic-threshold}).
The string-theoretic value $c = 26$ has
$\rho \approx 0.23$ (strongly convergent).

The near-alternation of
signs (Remark~\ref{rem:virasoro-shadow-generating-function}(i))
is quantified by the branch-point argument
$\arg(t_0)/\pi \in (0.91, 1)$, approaching~$1$ in the
semiclassical limit (Remark~\ref{rem:virasoro-shadow-generating-function}(iv)).  The exponent~$-5/2$ in the
asymptotics
$S_r \sim A\,\rho^r\,r^{-5/2}\cos(r\theta + \varphi)$
is universal (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-radius}(ii)):
it reflects the square-root singularity of~$\sqrt{Q_L}$ at
the branch points, not the specific Virasoro OPE data.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Complementarity potential]
\label{rem:virasoro-complementarity-potential}
\index{complementarity potential!Virasoro}
The complementarity potential
$S_{\mathrm{Vir}}(x) = \sum_{r=2}^\infty \frac{1}{2r}\,
\mathrm{Sh}_r\,x^r$ through septic order is
\begin{align*}
S_{\mathrm{Vir}}(x)
&= \frac{c}{4}\,x^2
+ \frac{1}{3}\,x^3
+ \frac{5}{12\,c(5c{+}22)}\,x^4
- \frac{2}{5\,c^2(5c{+}22)}\,x^5 \\
&\quad + \frac{45c{+}193}{27\,c^3(5c{+}22)^2}\,x^6
- \frac{4(15c{+}61)}{49\,c^4(5c{+}22)^2}\,x^7
+ O(x^8).
\end{align*}
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Finite termination for primitive archetypes; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-finite-termination}
\index{shadow tower!finite termination}
For the three frame families, the shadow tower terminates at finite arity:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textbf{Heisenberg:} $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\mathcal H)=0$ for all
  $r\ge 3$.  The tower terminates at arity~$2$: it is exactly Gaussian.

\item \textbf{Affine $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$
  \textup{(strict sector, minimal gauge):}}
  $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\mathrm{aff})=0$ for $r\ge 4$.  The tower terminates
  at arity~$3$.

\item \textbf{$\beta\gamma$ \textup{(weight-changing line):}}
  $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\beta\gamma)|_L=0$ for $r\ge 3$ by rank-one abelian
  rigidity.  The tower terminates at arity~$4$ on the
  weight-changing line.
\end{enumerate}
Virasoro is the first genuinely infinite tower:
$\mathrm{Sh}_r(\mathrm{Vir})\neq 0$ for all $r\ge 3$ for generic~$c$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For each primitive archetype, finite termination follows from vanishing
of all obstruction sources at the relevant arity.  For the Heisenberg,
all higher brackets vanish (the OPE is quadratic, so no composite
fields appear).  For affine $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$, the Jacobiator
vanishes and the quartic gauge freedom absorbs all remaining terms.
For $\beta\gamma$, rank-one abelian rigidity
(Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-rank-one-rigidity}) gives vanishing on the
rank-one weight-changing line.

For Virasoro, Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced} gives
$\mathrm{Sh}_5\neq 0$.  Then $\mathfrak o^{(6)}$ contains
$\{\mathfrak C,\mathrm{Sh}_5\}\neq 0$, forcing
$\mathrm{Sh}_6\neq 0$, and so on by induction: the cubic vertex
$\mathfrak C=2x^3$ acts as a permanent source, and the non-polynomial
character of the complementarity potential is established.\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Shadow Postnikov tower interpretation]
\label{rem:w-postnikov-interpretation}
\index{shadow Postnikov tower!archetype classification}
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-finite-termination} classifies the
shadow Postnikov tower
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-postnikov-tower}) into
four archetype classes:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{llll}
\toprule
\emph{Archetype} & \emph{Termination arity} &
\emph{Obstruction mechanism} & \emph{Tower type} \\
\midrule
Heisenberg & $2$ (Gaussian) & no higher operations &
exact quadratic \\
Affine & $3$ (Lie) & Jacobi identity &
quadratic + cubic \\
$\beta\gamma$ & $4$ (contact) & rank-one rigidity &
quartic on weight line \\
Virasoro/$\mathcal{W}_N$ & $\infty$ & permanent cubic source &
non-polynomial \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
For families with infinite towers, the shadow Postnikov
tower does not converge at any finite arity: the full
limit $\Theta_\cA = \varprojlim_r
\Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:recursive-existence}) is genuinely
infinite-order.  This is the mathematical content of the
statement that the Virasoro complementarity potential is
non-polynomial.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Virasoro/$\mathcal{W}_N$ shadow Postnikov tower:
infinite; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:virasoro-postnikov-nontermination}
\index{shadow Postnikov tower!Virasoro non-termination}
The shadow Postnikov tower
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:shadow-postnikov-tower})}
of the Virasoro algebra \textup{(}and principal
$\mathcal{W}_N$ for $N \geq 2$\textup{)} does not terminate at
any finite arity:
$o_{r+1}(\mathrm{Vir}) \neq 0$ for all $r \geq 4$ for
generic~$c$.
Equivalently, $\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\leq r} \neq
\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\leq r-1}$ for all $r \geq 3$.
The permanent cubic source $\mathfrak{C}_{\mathrm{Vir}} = 2x^3$
drives the infinite tower.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from Theorems~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced}
and~\ref{thm:w-finite-termination}: the inductive mechanism
$\mathfrak{o}^{(r+1)} \ni
\{\mathfrak{C},\mathrm{Sh}_r\}_H \neq 0$
propagates non-vanishing to all arities.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Genus-$1$ Hessian correction for the Virasoro shadow}
\label{subsec:w-virasoro-genus1-hessian}
\index{genus loop operator!Virasoro computation}
\index{Hessian correction!genus-1 Virasoro}

The infinite shadow tower carries information beyond the
$\hat{A}$-genus.  The first concrete manifestation is the genus-$1$
Hessian correction obtained by applying the genus loop operator
$\Lambda_P$ (Definition~\ref{def:nms-genus-loop-operator}) to the
quartic shadow.  We give the self-contained computation here;
the abstract framework is developed in
Appendix~\ref{sec:nms-genus-loop-operator}.

\begin{theorem}[Genus-$1$ Hessian correction for Virasoro;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-virasoro-genus1-hessian}
\index{Virasoro algebra!genus-1 Hessian correction}
On the primary line with $H = (c/2)x^2$,
$\mathfrak C = 2x^3$,
$\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}} = Q_0\,x^4$ where
$Q_0 = 10/[c(5c+22)]$, one has:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The genus-$1$ Hessian correction is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-virasoro-genus1-hessian}
\delta H^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
= \Lambda_P\bigl(\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}\bigr)
= \frac{120}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^2.
\end{equation}

\item The genus-$1$ loop ratio is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-virasoro-loop-ratio}
\rho^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
:= \frac{\delta H^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}}{H^{(0)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}}
= \frac{240}{c^3(5c+22)}.
\end{equation}
This is a nontrivial rational function of $c$ that is not
determined by $\kappa = c/2$ alone.  Two algebras with the same
$\kappa$ but different $c$ are distinguished by
$\rho^{(1)}$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The computation proceeds in five steps.

\emph{Step~1} (Genus loop on rank-$1$ symmetric tensors).
On a one-dimensional primary slice $V = \mathbb C\langle x\rangle$
with Hessian $H = (c/2)x^2$, the propagator is $P = 2/c$.
The genus loop operator
$\Lambda_P \colon \operatorname{Sym}^r(V^*) \to
\operatorname{Sym}^{r-2}(V^*)$
contracts two symmetric legs with the propagator
(Definition~\ref{def:nms-genus-loop-operator}).  For a
rank-$r$ symmetric tensor $\alpha = \alpha_0\,x^r$, the
number of ways to choose the two legs to contract is
$\binom{r}{2}$, giving
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-genus-loop-rank1-formula}
\Lambda_P(\alpha_0\,x^r)
= \binom{r}{2} \cdot P \cdot \alpha_0 \cdot x^{r-2}.
\end{equation}

\emph{Step~2} (Apply to the quartic shadow).
With $r = 4$, $\alpha_0 = Q_0 = 10/[c(5c+22)]$, and
$P = 2/c$:
\[
\Lambda_P(Q_0\,x^4)
= \binom{4}{2} \cdot \frac{2}{c} \cdot
\frac{10}{c(5c+22)} \cdot x^2
= 6 \cdot \frac{2}{c} \cdot
\frac{10}{c(5c+22)} \cdot x^2
= \frac{120}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^2.
\]

\emph{Step~3} (Identify the genus-$1$ Hessian correction).
By the non-separating clutching law
(Corollary~\ref{cor:nms-genus-one-hessian-correction}),
the genus-$1$ correction to the Hessian in the one-vertex
sector is $\delta H^{(1)} = \Lambda_P(\mathfrak Q^{(0)})$.
Thus
\[
\delta H^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
= \frac{120}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^2.
\]

\emph{Step~4} (Compute the loop ratio).
\[
\rho^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
= \frac{\delta H^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}}{H^{(0)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}}
= \frac{120/[c^2(5c+22)] \cdot x^2}{(c/2)\,x^2}
= \frac{120}{c^2(5c+22)} \cdot \frac{2}{c}
= \frac{240}{c^3(5c+22)}.
\]

\emph{Step~5} (Apply to the cubic shadow).
With $r = 3$, $\alpha_0 = 2$, and $P = 2/c$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-virasoro-cubic-loop-computation}
\Lambda_P(\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{Vir}})
= \Lambda_P(2x^3)
= \binom{3}{2} \cdot \frac{2}{c} \cdot 2 \cdot x
= \frac{12}{c}\,x.
\end{equation}
This is the genus-$1$ correction to the linear term: a canonical
direction in $V^*$ determined by the cubic shadow and the
propagator.  It is the rank-$1$ analogue of the Weyl vector
direction detected by the affine cubic loop
(Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-genus-loop-model-families}(ii)).\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Tensorial vs.\ scalar modular invariants]
\label{rem:w-virasoro-tensorial-invariant}
\index{modular invariant!tensorial}
The genus-$1$ Hessian correction
$\delta H^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}} = 120/[c^2(5c+22)] \cdot x^2$
is a \emph{tensorial} modular invariant: it lives in
$\operatorname{Sym}^2(V^*)$ and is not determined by the scalar
curvature $\kappa = c/2$.  In particular, consider two hypothetical
chiral algebras $\cA$ and $\cA'$ with
$\kappa(\cA) = \kappa(\cA') = c/2$ but whose quartic contact
coefficients differ.  Then
$\delta H^{(1)}_{\cA} \neq \delta H^{(1)}_{\cA'}$:
the genus-$1$ modular homotopy theory distinguishes them even
though their $\hat{A}$-genera agree.  The loop ratio
$\rho^{(1)} = 240/[c^3(5c+22)]$ is the simplest numerical
invariant extracted from this tensorial data.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The infinite tower and modular information beyond
the $\hat{A}$-genus]
\label{rem:w-infinite-tower-beyond-ahat}
\index{shadow tower!infinite!modular information}
\index{A-hat genus@$\hat{A}$-genus!limitations}
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-finite-termination} reveals a fundamental structural
divide.  The primitive archetypes terminate: Gaussian at arity~$2$,
Lie/tree at arity~$3$, contact at arity~$4$.  Their complementarity
potentials $S_{\cA}$ are polynomial, and the information they encode
about the moduli space $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$ is captured by
finitely many tautological classes.

Virasoro is different.  The non-polynomial complementarity potential
$S_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ records an infinite sequence of tautological
invariants $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\mathrm{Vir})$ for $r=2,3,4,5,\dots$,
each capturing finer modular structure than the last.  This is the
mechanism by which the Virasoro modular package carries strictly more
information than the $\hat{A}$-genus: the $\hat{A}$-genus is
controlled by the scalar curvature $\kappa$ (arity~$2$) and a finite
number of Pontryagin-type corrections, whereas
$\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ encodes an infinite tower of genuinely new
invariants sourced by the cubic--quartic interaction.

More precisely, the all-arity master equation
\[
\nabla_{H_{\mathrm{Vir}}}(\mathrm{Sh}_r)
+\mathfrak o^{(r)}=0
\]
ensures that each $\mathrm{Sh}_r$ is determined by the lower-arity
data via the Poisson bracket with $\mathfrak C$ and
$\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}$.  The recursion never terminates
because $\mathfrak C\neq 0$ and $\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}\neq 0$
simultaneously --- the hallmark of a mixed family.  The same mechanism
applies to all principal $\mathcal{W}_N$ with $N\ge 3$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-principal-wn-contact-nonvanishing}), producing an
infinite tower for every member of the $\mathcal{W}$-algebra series.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}_3$}{W3} quintic obstruction}
\label{subsec:w-w3-quintic-obstruction}
\index{quintic obstruction!W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$}
\index{shadow tower!W3 infinite@$\mathcal{W}_3$ infinite}

The Virasoro quintic was forced by the interaction between the
rank-$1$ cubic $\mathfrak C = 2x^3$ and the rank-$1$ quartic
$\mathfrak Q = Q_0\,x^4$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced}).  For $\mathcal{W}_3$
the mechanism is richer: the two-generator primary slice supports
genuinely multi-variable obstructions.

\begin{proposition}[$\mathcal{W}_3$ quintic obstruction;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:w-w3-quintic-obstruction}
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!quintic obstruction}
On the two-generator primary slice of $\mathcal{W}_3$ with
coordinates $(t,w)$ dual to $(T,W)$, the quintic obstruction is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-w3-quintic-obstruction}
\mathfrak o^{(5)}_{W_3}
= \bigl\{\mathfrak C_{W_3},\,
\mathfrak Q_{W_3}\bigr\}_{H_{W_3}}
\neq 0
\qquad\text{for generic~$c$}.
\end{equation}
Consequently $\mathrm{Sh}_5(\mathcal{W}_3) \neq 0$ generically:
the $\mathcal{W}_3$ shadow tower is also infinite.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The cubic $\mathfrak C_{W_3} = 2t^3 + 3tw^2$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-w3-mixed-shadow}) is a nonzero polynomial of
degree~$3$ in $(t,w)$.  The quartic $\mathfrak Q_{W_3}$ contains
the weight-$4$ contact channel through~$\Lambda$ with coefficient
proportional to $32/(22+5c)$ as well as weight-$6$ contact
channels through $\Lambda_2$ and $\Lambda_3$.  In particular,
$\mathfrak Q_{W_3}\neq 0$ for generic~$c$.

The $H$-Poisson bracket on the primary slice with diagonal
propagator $P = \operatorname{diag}(2/c,\,3/c)$ is
\[
\bigl\{\mathfrak C,\,\mathfrak Q\bigr\}_{H}
= \frac{\partial\mathfrak C}{\partial t}\cdot \frac{2}{c}\cdot
\frac{\partial\mathfrak Q}{\partial t}
+ \frac{\partial\mathfrak C}{\partial w}\cdot \frac{3}{c}\cdot
\frac{\partial\mathfrak Q}{\partial w}.
\]
Since $\partial\mathfrak C/\partial t = 6t^2 + 3w^2$ and
$\partial\mathfrak C/\partial w = 6tw$, and the quartic gradients
are generically nonzero, the bracket is a degree-$5$ polynomial
in $(t,w)$ that does not vanish identically.  By the all-arity
master equation
(Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-all-arity-master-equation}),
$\nabla_H(\mathrm{Sh}_5) + \mathfrak o^{(5)} = 0$,
so $\mathrm{Sh}_5 \neq 0$.\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[$\mathcal{W}_3$ multi-channel tower: T-line autonomy and mixing]
\label{rem:w3-multi-channel-tower}
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!T-line autonomy}
\index{W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!mixing polynomial}
The $\mathcal{W}_3$ shadow tower on the $T$-line
($w = 0$, only stress-tensor insertions) is \emph{autonomous}:
it equals the single-variable Virasoro tower of
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-generating-function} exactly,
verified through arity~$10$.  The mechanism is that the $W$-line
alternating vanishing
(Corollary~\ref{cor:w-line-alternating-vanishing}) kills all
odd-$W$-leg contributions, and the even-$W$-leg terms decouple on
$w = 0$.

The \emph{mixing polynomial} (computational data from Proposition~\ref{thm:propagator-variance})
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-mixing-polynomial}
P(c) = 25c^2 + 100c - 428 = 25(c+2)^2 - 528
\end{equation}
controls arity-$6$ non-autonomy on the mixed lines.
Proposition~\ref{thm:propagator-variance} gives
$\delta(\mathcal{W}_3) = 0$ if and only if $P(c) = 0$, i.e.\
at $c = (-100 \pm \sqrt{100^2 + 4\cdot 25\cdot 428})/(2\cdot 25)
= -2 \pm 2\sqrt{132/25}$.
At these curvature-proportionality loci the multi-channel tower
collapses to a single effective channel at arity~$6$; for all other~$c$ the
$T$--$W$ mixing is irreducible and the diagonal tower differs from
the autonomous Virasoro tower starting at arity~$6$.

The $\mathcal{W}_3$ quintic nonvanishing
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w3-quintic-nonvanishing}) confirms that
$\mathcal{W}_3$ belongs to class~M ($r_{\max} = \infty$), matching
the Virasoro classification but with a richer multi-variable structure.
\end{remark}

\begin{example}[$\mathcal{W}_3$ shadow tower coefficients]
\label{ex:w3-shadow-coefficients}
\index{$\mathcal{W}_3$!shadow tower coefficients}
The two-channel shadow tower for $\mathcal{W}_3$ with generators $T$ (weight~$2$) and $W$ (weight~$3$), computed through arity~$6$ (\texttt{coxeter\_arity4\_deep.py}, $69$~tests):
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{cl}
\toprule
$r$ & $\mathrm{Sh}_r(x_T, x_W)$ \\
\midrule
$2$ & $\frac{c}{2}\,x_T^2 + \frac{c}{3}\,x_W^2$ \\[4pt]
$3$ & $2\,x_T^3 + 3\,x_T\,x_W^2$ \\[4pt]
$4$ & $\frac{10}{c(5c{+}22)}\,x_T^4 + \frac{960}{c(5c{+}22)^2}\,x_T^2 x_W^2 + \frac{2560}{c(5c{+}22)^3}\,x_W^4$ \\[4pt]
$5$ & $\frac{-48}{c^2(5c{+}22)}\,x_T^5
      - \frac{24(5c{+}262)}{c^2(5c{+}22)^2}\,x_T^3 x_W^2
      - \frac{1152(5c{+}38)}{c^2(5c{+}22)^3}\,x_T x_W^4$ \\[4pt]
$6$ & $\frac{80(45c{+}193)}{3c^3(5c{+}22)^2}\,x_T^6
      + \dotsb
      + \frac{64(5625c^4{+}117000c^3{+}\dotsb)}{c^3(5c{+}22)^6}\,x_W^6$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\noindent
The $T$-line restriction ($x_W = 0$) equals the Virasoro shadow tower identically at all computed arities (verified through $r = 10$).  Odd powers of $x_W$ vanish by $W$-parity.  The full $2$-D tower is computed through arity~$8$ ($21$~nonzero coefficients, each a closed-form rational function of~$c$).  All denominators factor as $c^a(5c{+}22)^b$: the Kac-shadow singularity principle holds on the full $2$-D deformation space, not just on~$1$-D projections.  The mixed coefficients (those with $x_T^a x_W^b$ for $0 < a, b$) are the genuinely new data invisible on either~$1$-D projection.
\end{example}

\begin{remark}[Coxeter anomaly]
\label{rem:coxeter-anomaly}
\index{Coxeter anomaly|textbf}
\index{$\mathcal{W}_3$!Coxeter anomaly}
The naive two-channel sewing of the cubic shadow (using only $T_{(1)}T = 2T$ and $T_{(1)}W = 3W$) predicts a quartic $S_4^{\mathrm{free}} = -9/(2c)$ on the $T$-line, missing the factor $(5c{+}22)$ in the denominator.  The actual quartic $10/[c(5c{+}22)]$ arises from the composite operator $\Lambda = {:}TT{:} - \tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2 T$ at conformal weight~$4$, whose exchange produces the Kac-determinant factor.  The difference $(45c{+}218)/[2c(5c{+}22)]$ is the \emph{Coxeter anomaly}: the quartic contact contribution from composite operators not captured by the strong-generator OPE alone.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[$\mathcal{W}_3$ $W$-line structure and inter-channel coupling]
\label{rem:w3-w-line}
\label{rem:w3-interchannel-coupling}
\index{$\mathcal{W}_3$!$W$-line shadow}
\index{inter-channel coupling|textbf}
\index{shadow tower!inter-channel coupling}
On the $W$-line ($x_T = 0$): $\mathrm{Sh}_r = 0$ for odd~$r$ ($W$-parity).  The even-arity tower $S_2^W = c/3$, $S_4^W = 2560/[c(5c{+}22)^3]$ does \emph{not} follow the single-line $\sqrt{Q}$ structure (Theorem~\ref{thm:riccati-algebraicity}): the $W$-line is non-autonomous, receiving backreaction from the $T$-channel through cross-derivatives in the $2$-D H-Poisson bracket.  This contrasts with the exact autonomy of the $T$-line.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Inter-channel coupling mechanism.}\;
At arity~$6$ the obstruction on the $W$-line receives a $T$-channel correction
absent from the autonomous $1$-D recursion.
The cubic shadow $\mathrm{Sh}_3 = 2x_T^3 + 3x_T x_W^2$ has
$(\partial_{x_T} \mathrm{Sh}_3)|_{x_T = 0} = 3 x_W^2 \neq 0$:
it has a nonvanishing \emph{normal derivative} on the $W$-line.
The quintic shadow $\mathrm{Sh}_5$ has an $(x_T^1 x_W^4)$-component
$S_{1,4} = -1152(5c{+}38)/[c^2(5c{+}22)^3]$ whose normal derivative
is $S_{1,4}\,x_W^4$.  The $T$-channel bracket
$\{\mathrm{Sh}_3,\mathrm{Sh}_5\}^T|_{x_T = 0} = (3x_W^2)(2/c)(S_{1,4}\,x_W^4)$
contributes an arity-$6$ correction
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w3-interchannel-correction}
  \delta_6^{W\text{-line}}
  \;=\;
  \frac{576(5c+38)}{c^3(5c+22)^3}
\end{equation}
to the $W$-line sextic shadow, shifting it from the autonomous value $-13107200/[c^3(5c{+}22)^6]$ to the full value.  The autonomous $W$-line recursion misses this entirely.  At arity~$8$ and higher, further $T$-channel corrections enter through $\{\mathrm{Sh}_3, \mathrm{Sh}_7\}^T$, $\{\mathrm{Sh}_5, \mathrm{Sh}_5\}^T$, etc.

The coupling correction~\eqref{eq:w3-interchannel-correction} vanishes on any direction~$L$ in the deformation space where the propagator variance $\delta_{\mathrm{mix}} = 0$ (Proposition~\ref{thm:propagator-variance}).  The $T$-line is autonomous precisely because it has no transverse normal derivatives to couple to.  More generally, a subline of the deformation space is autonomous at arity~$6$ if and only if it lies in the kernel of the propagator variance form.
\end{remark}

%% ---------------------------------------------------------------
\section{The \texorpdfstring{$N\!=\!1$}{N=1} super-Virasoro PVA and 3d supergravity}
\label{sec:super-virasoro-pva}
\index{super-Virasoro algebra!PVA}
\index{supergravity!3d holomorphic-topological}

The Virasoro PVA of
\S\ref{subsec:virasoro-teichmuller-phase-space} admits an $N=1$
supersymmetric extension.  The associated 3d theory is a
holomorphic-topological supergravity.

\begin{definition}[$N=1$ super-Virasoro PVA;
\ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere{} \cite{KhanZeng25}]
\label{def:super-virasoro-pva}
\index{super-Virasoro algebra!lambda-bracket@$\lambda$-bracket}
The \emph{$N=1$ super-Virasoro Poisson vertex algebra} is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:super-vir-pva}
\mathcal{P}_{\mathrm{sVir}}
= \operatorname{Sym}\!\bigl(\mathbb{C}[\partial]T
  \oplus \mathbb{C}[\partial]G\bigr),
\end{equation}
where $T$ has conformal weight~$2$ (stress tensor) and $G$ has
weight~$\tfrac{3}{2}$ (supercurrent), with $\lambda$-brackets
\begin{align}
\{T_\lambda T\}
  &= \partial T + 2T\lambda + \tfrac{c}{12}\lambda^3,
  \label{eq:svir-TT}\\
\{T_\lambda G\}
  &= \partial G + \tfrac{3}{2}\,G\lambda,
  \label{eq:svir-TG}\\
\{G_\lambda G\}
  &= 2T + \tfrac{c}{3}\lambda^2.
  \label{eq:svir-GG}
\end{align}
The bracket $\{G_\lambda G\} = 2T + \frac{c}{3}\lambda^2$ is the
classical $\lambda$-bracket encoding: the stress tensor is the
square of the supercurrent.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[3d HT supergravity action;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{prop:super-virasoro-3d-action}
\index{supergravity!3d HT action}
The 3d holomorphic-topological supergravity associated to
$\mathcal{P}_{\mathrm{sVir}}$ has fields $(\mu,T)$ of spins
$(2,-1)$ and $(\chi,G)$ of spins $(\frac{3}{2},-\frac{1}{2})$ on
$M = \mathbb{R}_t \times \Sigma$, with action
\begin{multline}\label{eq:super-virasoro-3d-action}
  S_{\mathrm{sVir}}
  \;=\;
  \int \mu\,(dt + \bar\partial)\,T
  \;+\;
  \chi\,(dt + \bar\partial)\,G \\
  +\;\int\!\Bigl(
    T\mu\partial\mu
    + \tfrac{c}{24}\,\mu\,\partial^3\mu
    + \tfrac{3}{2}\,G\chi\partial\mu
    + (\partial G)\chi\mu
    + 2T\chi^2
    + \tfrac{c}{3}\,\chi\,\partial^2\chi
  \Bigr).
\end{multline}
The supercurrent coupling $2T\chi^2$ and the gravitino kinetic
correction $\frac{c}{3}\chi\partial^2\chi$ are read off from the
$\{G_\lambda G\}$ bracket~\eqref{eq:svir-GG} by the standard
Poisson-sigma-model dictionary of~\cite{KhanZeng25}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Slab reduction and supersymmetric central-charge shift]
\label{rem:super-vir-slab-reduction}
\index{slab reduction!super-Virasoro}
\index{central charge!supersymmetric shift}
Under slab reduction, the super-Virasoro theory decomposes into a
spin-$(2,-1)$ $\beta\gamma$ system ($c(2) = 26$ by
equation~\eqref{eq:w3-central-charge-formula}) and a
spin-$(\frac{3}{2},-\frac{1}{2})$ $\beta\gamma$ system
($c(\frac{3}{2}) = 11$), giving $c_{\mathrm{slab}} = 37$.  The quantum
$N=1$ super-Virasoro algebra appears at the shifted central charge
\begin{equation}\label{eq:svir-ceff}
  c_{\mathrm{eff}} = c + \tfrac{37}{2}.
\end{equation}
The complementarity pairing for the super-Virasoro algebra
is $c + c' = 37$, the supersymmetric analogue of the bosonic
Virasoro pairing $c + c' = 26$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Supersymmetric shadow tower]
\label{rem:super-virasoro-shadow-tower}
\index{shadow tower!super-Virasoro}
The shadow tower of the $N=1$ super-Virasoro algebra inherits a
$\mathbb{Z}/2$-grading from the supercurrent~$G$.  The bracket
$\{G_\lambda G\} = 2T + \frac{c}{3}\lambda^2$ ensures that the
gravitino sector does not generate independent quartic obstructions:
the quartic contact invariant
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{sVir}}$ factorises through the
bosonic Virasoro quartic of
\S\ref{subsec:w-virasoro-quartic-explicit}.  This is the
shadow-calculus manifestation of supersymmetric non-renormalization.
The $N=1$ extension amounts to
enlarging the graph-sum data of
$\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$~\eqref{eq:modular-bar-hamiltonian} by
half-integer-spin propagators $P_G$ for the supercurrent; the
supersymmetric Ward identity forces the $G$-channel graphs to
factor through the $T$-channel, preserving the projection structure
of Remark~\ref{rem:five-from-one}.
\end{remark}


%% ---------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Semistrict modular higher-spin geometry}
\label{sec:semistrict-modular-higher-spin}
\index{semistrictity!higher-spin geometry}
\index{W-algebra@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra!semistrict envelope}

The Virasoro shadow tower is infinite
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced}): the quintic
obstruction is nonzero, and so is every subsequent order
generically.  One might therefore expect that the \emph{bulk}
deformation algebra controlling the $\mathcal{W}_3$ sector is
equally wild --- an infinite sequence of higher operations $\ell_n$
with no structural simplification.  The truth is the reverse.  The
classical $\mathcal{W}_3$ Poisson vertex
algebra~\eqref{eq:w3-pva} has nonlinear generator-degree exactly
two: the only non-polynomial coefficient in the $\lambda$-brackets
is the $T^2$ term in $\{W_\lambda W\}$, which is quadratic in
generators.  The associated three-dimensional
holomorphic-topological Poisson sigma model therefore has a BV
differential that terminates at cubic order.  The resulting cyclic
$L_\infty$-algebra has $\ell_n = 0$ for $n \ge 4$.  This is
semistrictity: an infinite shadow tower generated by a
\emph{finite-arity} bulk.

The paradox is precise and structurally loaded.  The shadow tower
records the nonlinear deformation theory of a moduli problem
organized by graph sums with arbitrarily many vertices.  When the
bulk interaction has only two- and three-valent vertices, a single
trivalent graph can be iterated to produce arbitrarily high contact
orders --- but the local interaction data at each vertex remains
ternary.  The infinite tower is not a consequence of infinite
interaction complexity; it is a consequence of iterated
\emph{finite} complexity.  This is the structural mechanism behind
every ``higher-spin gravity is finite-valent at each vertex but
infinite in diagram count'' statement in the physics literature.

\subsection{Nonlinear generator-degree and finite-arity theorems}
\label{subsec:semistrict-finite-arity}

\begin{definition}[Nonlinear generator-degree]
\label{def:w-nonlinear-generator-degree}
\index{nonlinear generator-degree}
Let $V$ be a freely generated Poisson vertex algebra on generators
$u_i$.  The \emph{nonlinear generator-degree} of~$V$ is the maximal
number of generator factors appearing in any monomial of any
$\lambda$-bracket coefficient $\{u_i{}_\lambda u_j\}$, taken over all
pairs $(i,j)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Higher-spin envelope]
\label{def:w-higher-spin-envelope}
\index{higher-spin envelope}
Let $V$ be a freely generated Poisson vertex algebra, and let
$\mathfrak{M}_V$ be the formal moduli problem at the vacuum of the
three-dimensional holomorphic-topological Poisson sigma model
attached to~$V$.  Write
\[
Q_{\mathrm{BV}} = \sum_{n \ge 1} Q_n
\]
for the Taylor expansion of the BV homological vector field into
homogeneous polynomial components of degree~$n$.  The
\emph{higher-spin envelope} of~$V$ is the completed cyclic
$L_\infty$-algebra
\[
\operatorname{HS}(V)
\]
whose $n$-ary bracket $\ell_n$ is the shifted multilinear operation
corresponding to~$Q_n$.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Finite-arity theorem for polynomial PVAs;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-finite-arity-polynomial-pva}
\index{finite-arity theorem!polynomial PVA}
Let $V$ be a freely generated Poisson vertex algebra of nonlinear
generator-degree at most~$d$.  Then $\operatorname{HS}(V)$ is a
completed cyclic $L_\infty$-algebra with
\[
\ell_n = 0 \qquad \text{for all } n > d+1.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The BV differential of the associated Poisson sigma model has the
schematic form
\[
Q_{\mathrm{BV}}\Phi^i
= d_{\mathrm{HT}}\Phi^i + \Pi^{ij}(\partial,\Phi)\,\eta_j,
\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{BV}}\eta_i
= d_{\mathrm{HT}}\eta_i
+ \tfrac{1}{2}\sum_{n \ge 0}(-\partial)^n \eta_j\,
\frac{\partial\Pi^{jk}(\partial,\Phi)}{\partial(\partial^n\Phi^i)}\,\eta_k,
\]
where $\Pi$ records the $\lambda$-bracket coefficients of~$V$; compare
\cite[\S3]{KhanZeng25}.  If every coefficient of~$\Pi$ has nonlinear
generator-degree at most~$d$, then the first formula is polynomial of
total degree at most $d+1$: a degree-$\le d$ coefficient multiplies
one ghost~$\eta_j$.  In the second formula, differentiation with
respect to a field or jet variable reduces the field degree by one,
while multiplication by two ghosts raises the total degree by two;
hence this expression also has total degree at most $d+1$.  Therefore
$Q_n = 0$ for $n > d+1$, whence $\ell_n = 0$ for $n > d+1$.  Since
$Q_{\mathrm{BV}}^2 = 0$, the brackets satisfy the $L_\infty$
identities, and since $Q_{\mathrm{BV}}$ is Hamiltonian for the BV
pairing, the algebra is cyclic.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Semistrictity of the classical $\mathcal{W}_3$
bulk; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:w-semistrictity-classical-w3}
\index{semistrictity!classical W3@classical $\mathcal{W}_3$}
The higher-spin envelope of the classical $\mathcal{W}_3$ PVA
satisfies
\[
\ell_n = 0 \qquad (n \ge 4).
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The only nonlinear monomials in the classical $\mathcal{W}_3$
$\lambda$-brackets are the $T^2$ and $T\partial T$ terms in
$\{W_\lambda W\}$~\eqref{eq:w3-WW-bracket}: these have
generator-degree~$2$.  Apply
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-finite-arity-polynomial-pva} with $d = 2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Paradox resolved]
\label{rem:w-semistrict-paradox}
\index{shadow tower!infinite from semistrict bulk}
Corollary~\ref{cor:w-semistrictity-classical-w3} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-virasoro-quintic-forced} together sharpen the
picture.  The Virasoro shadow tower is infinite --- the quintic, sextic,
and all higher shadows are generically nonzero --- yet the bulk
$\operatorname{HS}(\mathcal{W}_3^{\mathrm{cl}})$ has only $\ell_1$,
$\ell_2$, and $\ell_3$.  The resolution is that the shadow tower at
arity~$r$ records \emph{graph sums} with $r$ external legs, assembled
from trivalent and quadrivalent vertices by iterated contraction.  Each
vertex is controlled by $\ell_2$ or $\ell_3$, but the number of
vertices in a connected graph is unbounded.  Thus finite bulk arity
produces infinite shadow complexity through iterated interaction, not
through local interaction at a single vertex.  This is the precise
algebraic content of ``the Virasoro tower is mixed cubic-quartic'' in
the archetype trichotomy of
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-archetype-trichotomy}.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Tree identities and graph finiteness}
\label{subsec:semistrict-tree-identities}

\begin{proposition}[Tree identity for semistrict cyclic theories;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:w-semistrict-tree-identity}
\index{tree identity!semistrict theory}
Let $L$ be a semistrict cyclic $L_\infty$-algebra (i.e.\
$\ell_n = 0$ for $n \ge 4$).  A connected tree-level Feynman graph
with $n$ external legs, $v_3$ trivalent interaction vertices, and
$v_4$ quadrivalent interaction vertices satisfies
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-semistrict-tree-identity}
2v_3 + 3v_4 = n - 2.
\end{equation}
In particular, only finitely many interaction trees contribute at
fixed~$n$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $e$ be the number of internal edges.  For a connected tree,
$e = v_3 + v_4 - 1$.  Counting half-edges gives
$3v_3 + 4v_4 = 2e + n$.  Substituting the tree relation yields
\[
3v_3 + 4v_4 = 2(v_3 + v_4 - 1) + n,
\]
which simplifies to~\eqref{eq:w-semistrict-tree-identity}.  Integer
pairs $(v_3, v_4)$ satisfying this are finite for fixed~$n$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Stable-graph identity for semistrict modular
theories; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:w-semistrict-stable-graph}
\index{stable graph!semistrict identity}
Let $\Gamma$ be a connected stable graph contributing to a modular
semistrict cyclic $L_\infty$-theory, with total genus~$g$, $n$
external legs, vertex genera~$g(v)$, and $v_k$ vertices of valence
$k \in \{3,4\}$.  Then
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-semistrict-stable-graph}
v_3 + 2v_4 + 2\sum_{v \in V(\Gamma)} g(v) = n + 2g - 2.
\end{equation}
In particular, $v_3 + 2v_4 \le n + 2g - 2$, and only finitely many
stable graphs contribute at fixed $(g,n)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $E(\Gamma)$ and $V(\Gamma)$ denote the edge and vertex sets, and
let $k_v$ be the valence of vertex~$v$.  Since each internal edge
contributes two half-edges,
$\sum_v k_v = 2|E(\Gamma)| + n$.  Hence
\[
\sum_v (k_v - 2) = n + 2\bigl(|E(\Gamma)| - |V(\Gamma)| + 1\bigr)
- 2.
\]
Now $b_1(\Gamma) = |E(\Gamma)| - |V(\Gamma)| + 1$ and
$g = b_1(\Gamma) + \sum_v g(v)$, so
\[
\sum_v (k_v - 2) = n + 2g - 2 - 2\sum_v g(v).
\]
Since every interaction vertex has valence $3$ or~$4$, the left-hand
side equals $v_3 + 2v_4$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Cubic weight recursion around the shadow base point}
\label{subsec:semistrict-cubic-recursion}

The graph finiteness theorems above imply that the modular lift
problem for $\mathcal{W}_3$ is not an amorphous infinity of coherence
data.  It is a filtered cubic recursion, controlled by the
reduced-weight windows $K_q(\mathcal{W}_3)$
(Definition~\ref{def:finite-window}).  The corrected Koszul recursion
$h_q = 2h_{q-1} + h_{q-2} + h_{q-3}$ (reflecting the cumulant
cogenerator $\Lambda^*$) replaces the naive
$h_q = 2h_{q-1} + h_{q-2}$, with window sizes
$1, 3, 8, 20, 51, 130, \ldots$ and completion entropy
$h_K(\mathcal{W}_3) \approx 0.772$
(\S\ref{sec:w-completion-kinematics}).

\begin{definition}[Weighted modular semistrict envelope of
$\mathcal{W}_3$]
\label{def:w-weighted-modular-envelope}
\index{modular envelope!weighted semistrict}
Define
\[
L_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{mod}}
:=
\bigl(\operatorname{HS}(\mathcal{W}_3^{\mathrm{cl}})
\oplus \mathbb{k}\varepsilon\bigr)
\,\widehat{\otimes}\,\mathcal{H}_\lambda,
\]
where $\mathcal{H}_\lambda = \widehat{\operatorname{Sym}}
\bigl(\bigoplus_{g \ge 1}\mathbb{k}\,\sigma_g\bigr)$ is the
completed Hodge-shadow coefficient algebra with $\sigma_g$ primitive
of weight $\operatorname{wt}(\sigma_g) = 2g$, and $\varepsilon$ is a
closed central element of degree~$1$ and weight~$0$.  Assign conformal
weights $\operatorname{wt}(\partial^m T) = m+2$,
$\operatorname{wt}(\partial^m W) = m+3$.  Let $F^N$ be the closed span
of monomials of total weight $\ge N$.  The distinguished central
shadow base point is
\[
\Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}}
:= \kappa(\mathcal{W}_3)\,\varepsilon \otimes \sum_{g \ge 1}\sigma_g.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Admissibility of the weight filtration;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:w-semistrict-admissibility}
The filtration $F^\bullet L_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{mod}}$ is
complete, separated, and admissible:
\[
\ell_1(F^N) \subseteq F^N,
\qquad
\ell_2(F^i, F^j) \subseteq F^{i+j},
\qquad
\ell_3(F^i, F^j, F^k) \subseteq F^{i+j+k}.
\]
Each weight slice $F^N/F^{N+1}$ is finite-dimensional.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The differential $\ell_1$ is the linearized BV differential and
preserves weight.  The brackets $\ell_2$ and $\ell_3$ are built from
the polynomial $\lambda$-bracket coefficients
of~\eqref{eq:w3-TT-bracket}--\eqref{eq:w3-WW-bracket}, which can
only add weights.  The weight slice at level~$N$ is spanned by
jet monomials in $T$ and $W$ of total weight~$N$ tensored with
Hodge-shadow monomials of complementary weight: both sets are finite,
being partitions of a fixed integer.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Cubic weight recursion; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-cubic-weight-recursion}
\index{cubic weight recursion!W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$}
Write a putative modular lift in the form
$\Theta = \Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}} + \alpha$ with
$\alpha = \sum_{N \ge 1}\alpha_N$ and
$\alpha_N \in F^N/F^{N+1}$.  Then
$\Theta \in \operatorname{MC}(L_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{mod}})$ if
and only if, for every $N \ge 1$,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-cubic-weight-recursion}
\ell_1(\alpha_N)
= -\frac{1}{2}\sum_{i+j=N}\pi_N\ell_2(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)
  -\frac{1}{6}\sum_{i+j+k=N}\pi_N\ell_3(\alpha_i,\alpha_j,\alpha_k),
\end{equation}
where $\pi_N \colon F^N \to F^N/F^{N+1}$ is the quotient map.  Each
stage is a finite linear equation in~$\alpha_N$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since $\Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}}$ is closed and central,
the Maurer--Cartan equation for $\Theta$ reduces to
\[
\ell_1(\alpha) + \tfrac{1}{2}\ell_2(\alpha,\alpha)
+ \tfrac{1}{6}\ell_3(\alpha,\alpha,\alpha) = 0.
\]
This uses $\ell_n = 0$ for $n \ge 4$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:w-semistrictity-classical-w3}).  Expanding
$\alpha = \sum_N \alpha_N$ and projecting to weight~$N$ gives
\eqref{eq:w-cubic-weight-recursion} by admissibility
(Proposition~\ref{prop:w-semistrict-admissibility}).  Finiteness of
each stage follows from finite-dimensionality of $F^N/F^{N+1}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Cubic obstruction classes; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:w-cubic-obstruction-classes}
\index{obstruction class!cubic semistrict}
At weight~$N$, the obstruction to solving
\eqref{eq:w-cubic-weight-recursion} lies in
$H^2(F^N/F^{N+1}, \ell_1)$ and depends polynomially of degree at
most three on the lower-weight coefficients
$\alpha_1, \dots, \alpha_{N-1}$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The right-hand side of~\eqref{eq:w-cubic-weight-recursion} is
$\ell_1$-closed by the semistrict $L_\infty$ identities.  Its class
in $H^2(F^N/F^{N+1}, \ell_1)$ vanishes if and only if the weight-$N$
coefficient can be chosen.  Since only $\ell_2$ and $\ell_3$ appear,
the dependence on lower-weight data is at most cubic.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The completed boundary model}
\label{subsec:semistrict-boundary-model}

\begin{definition}[Completed boundary model]
\label{def:w-completed-boundary-model}
\index{completed boundary model}
Let $L$ be a positively weighted, complete, semistrict cyclic
$L_\infty$-algebra with finite-dimensional weight slices.  Its
\emph{completed boundary model} is the complete dg algebra
\[
\operatorname{Bdy}(L)
:= \widehat{\operatorname{CE}}^\bullet(\tau_{>0}L)
= \prod_{m \ge 0}
   \operatorname{Sym}^m\!\bigl((\tau_{>0}L[1])^\vee\bigr),
\]
with continuous differential $d_{\mathrm{CE}} = d_1 + d_2 + d_3$
dual to the coderivation determined by $\ell_1$, $\ell_2$,
and~$\ell_3$.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Well-definedness; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:w-boundary-model-well-defined}
$\operatorname{Bdy}(\operatorname{HS}(\mathcal{W}_3^{\mathrm{cl}}))$
is a well-defined complete dg algebra.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Positive-weight truncation has finite-dimensional weight slices
(Proposition~\ref{prop:w-semistrict-admissibility}), so the graded
dual and completed symmetric algebra are defined weightwise.  The maps
dual to $\ell_1$, $\ell_2$, $\ell_3$ are continuous because these
brackets preserve positive weight and raise filtration.  Since the
semistrict $L_\infty$ identities give $d_{\mathrm{CE}}^2 = 0$, the
result is a complete dg algebra.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The semistrict modular higher-spin package}
\label{subsec:semistrict-package}

\begin{theorem}[The $\mathcal{W}_3$ semistrict modular higher-spin
package; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-semistrict-package}
\index{semistrict modular higher-spin package!W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$}
The classical $\mathcal{W}_3$ PVA canonically determines a
semistrict modular higher-spin package
\[
\mathfrak{P}_{\mathcal{W}_3}
