= \bigl(\mathcal{W}_3^{\mathrm{cl}},\,
         \operatorname{HS}(\mathcal{W}_3^{\mathrm{cl}}),\,
         \Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}},\,
         \operatorname{Bdy}(\mathcal{W}_3)\bigr)
\]
with the following properties:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The shadow base point
$\Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}}
= \kappa(\mathcal{W}_3)\,\varepsilon \otimes \sum_{g \ge 1}\sigma_g$
is a canonical Maurer--Cartan element.

\item The bulk envelope is cyclic and semistrict:
$\ell_n = 0$ for $n \ge 4$.

\item Translation by $\Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}}$
identifies the Maurer--Cartan fiber of fixed central shadow with the
Maurer--Cartan set of the noncentral sector.

\item Every modular lift is governed by the cubic weight recursion
of Theorem~\ref{thm:w-cubic-weight-recursion}; each obstruction is
finite-dimensional and at most cubic in lower-weight data.

\item Tree-level and higher-genus graph expansions are finite at
fixed external data, controlled by
\[
2v_3 + 3v_4 = n - 2
\qquad\text{(trees)},
\qquad
v_3 + 2v_4 + 2\sum_v g(v) = n + 2g - 2
\qquad\text{(stable graphs)}.
\]

\item The completed boundary model
$\operatorname{Bdy}(\mathcal{W}_3)$ is a well-defined complete dg
algebra.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\leavevmode
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Since $\varepsilon$ is closed and central, the MC equation for
$\Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}}$ holds identically.

\item Corollary~\ref{cor:w-semistrictity-classical-w3}.

\item Since $\Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}}$ is central, the
MC equation for
$\Theta_{\mathcal{W}_3}^{\mathrm{sh}} + \alpha$ reduces to the MC
equation for~$\alpha$ in the noncentral sector.

\item Proposition~\ref{prop:w-semistrict-admissibility} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-cubic-weight-recursion}.

\item Propositions~\ref{prop:w-semistrict-tree-identity}
and~\ref{prop:w-semistrict-stable-graph}.

\item Proposition~\ref{prop:w-boundary-model-well-defined}.
\qedhere
\end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[Finite-arity principle for principal
$\mathcal{W}_N$; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:w-finite-arity-WN}
\index{finite-arity principle!principal WN@principal $\mathcal{W}_N$}
For the classical principal $\mathcal{W}_N$ Poisson vertex algebra,
the higher-spin envelope satisfies
\[
\ell_n = 0 \qquad (n > N),
\]
i.e.\ the bulk is $N$-strict.  The modular lift around the canonical
central shadow base point is governed by a weight recursion involving
only the brackets $\ell_1, \dots, \ell_N$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proposition}[Miura arity bound is sharp]
\label{prop:miura-arity-sharp}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{Miura transform!arity bound sharpness}
\index{principal W-algebra@principal $\mathcal{W}$-algebra!Miura arity bound}
For each $N = 2, \ldots, 20$, the maximum generator-degree in the
principal $\mathcal{W}_N$ Poisson vertex algebra equals $N - 1$,
attained at the $\mathcal{W}^{(N)} \times \mathcal{W}^{(N)}$
self-OPE.  The Miura transform from the free-field realization gives
arity cutoff exactly at~$N$: $\ell_n = 0$ for $n > N$ at the PVA
level.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leavevmode
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Free-field realization.}
The Miura transform expresses each generator
$W^{(s)} \in \mathcal{W}_N$ ($s = 2, \ldots, N$) as the $s$-th
elementary symmetric differential polynomial in the free fields
$\partial\phi_1, \ldots, \partial\phi_N$.  Since $W^{(s)}$ is a
polynomial of degree~$s$ in the $\partial\phi_i$, the OPE
$\{W^{(s)}{}_\lambda W^{(s')}\}$ in the PVA produces composite
fields of degree at most $s + s' - 2$ in the free fields (each
contraction reduces the total degree by~$2$, and at least one
contraction is required).

\item \emph{Maximum generator-degree.}
The $\{W^{(N)}{}_\lambda W^{(N)}\}$ self-OPE produces composites of
maximum free-field degree $2N - 2$.  Re-expressing these composites
via Miura inversion: the highest generator-degree monomial is
$W^{(N-1)} \cdot (\text{lower-weight terms})$, contributing at
generator-degree $N - 1$.  No composite of generator-degree $\geq N$
can appear because such a composite would require free-field degree
$\geq N + 1$ from at least one factor, exceeding the available
degree~$N$.

\item \emph{Arity cutoff.}
The $n$-ary bracket $\ell_n$ in the PVA arises from the $(n-1)$-fold
iterated OPE.  By~(ii), each OPE step produces composites of
generator-degree at most $N - 1$.  An $n$-ary bracket with $n > N$
would require a composite of generator-degree $\geq N$ as an
intermediate, which cannot occur.  Hence $\ell_n = 0$ for $n > N$.

\item \emph{Sharpness.}
It remains to verify $\ell_N \neq 0$.  At $N = 2$, $\ell_2 \neq 0$
is the Virasoro OPE itself.  At $N = 3$, $\ell_3 \neq 0$ is the
cubic $\mathcal{W}_3$ bracket
\textup{(}Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:w-semistrictity-classical-w3})}.
For $N = 4, \ldots, 20$, the free-field realization gives an
explicit nonzero contribution to $\ell_N$: the fully contracted
$N$-point function
$\langle W^{(2)} \cdots W^{(2)} \rangle_{\text{Miura}}$ \textup{(}$N$
insertions of the stress tensor\textup{)} is a sum over pairings of
the $N$ free-field bilinears, yielding $(2N-1)!! \neq 0$.
\qedhere
\end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Evidence for the finite-arity principle]
\label{rem:w-finite-arity-evidence}
For $N = 2$ (Virasoro), the PVA has generator-degree~$1$ in the
single generator~$T$, so
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-finite-arity-polynomial-pva} gives $\ell_n = 0$
for $n \ge 3$: the bulk is strictly quadratic.  For $N = 3$,
Corollary~\ref{cor:w-semistrictity-classical-w3} gives semistrictity.
For general~$N$, the nonlinear generator-degree in the
$\{W^{(s)}{}_\lambda W^{(s')}\}$ brackets is bounded by $N-1$ (the
highest-weight composite has at most $N-1$ generator factors in the
free-field realization).  The conjecture asserts that this rough bound
is sharp.  Combined with the Hessian and cubic data of
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-principal-wn-hessian-cubic}, the $N$-strictness
conjecture would reduce the entire modular $\mathcal{W}_N$ problem to
a bounded recursion with finitely many graph types at each stage.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Connection to the shadow archetype classification]
\label{rem:w-semistrict-archetype-connection}
The archetype trichotomy
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-archetype-trichotomy}) classifies the shadow
tower \emph{through quartic order}.  The semistrict package
provides the complementary datum: the \emph{bulk arity} that
generates those shadows.  For the Heisenberg atom, bulk arity is~$2$
and the shadow terminates.  For affine $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$,
bulk arity is~$3$ (the Lie bracket) and the shadow terminates at
weight~$3$.  For $\beta\gamma$, bulk arity is~$3$ (from the contact
quartic plus the OPE structure) and the shadow terminates at
weight~$4$.  For Virasoro and $\mathcal{W}_3$, bulk arity
is~$3$ but the shadow tower is infinite --- the semistrict
package explains exactly how: by iterated trivalent contraction.
The finite-arity principle for $\mathcal{W}_N$ predicts that the
bulk arity grows to~$N$, but the shadow tower remains infinite for
all $N \ge 2$.
\end{remark}


%% ---------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Subregular W-algebras and completed Koszulity}
\label{sec:subregular-completed-koszulity}
\index{W-algebra@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra!subregular family}
\index{completed Koszulity}

Every principal $W$-algebra $\mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g},
f_{\mathrm{prin}})$ at generic level is \emph{completed Koszul}: the
completed bar spectral sequence collapses at~$E_1$, and the bar
homology is an exterior coalgebra on the suspended generators.  This
is a formal consequence of the PBW theorem and the Slodowy slice
geometry (Definition~\ref{def:classical-ds}), with no assumption on
the nilpotent orbit.

The subregular family $\mathcal{W}_n^{(2)}$ --- the hook-type
$W$-algebras attached to the subregular nilpotent in
$\mathfrak{sl}_n$ --- displays a different phenomenon: the homotopy
arity grows with~$n$.  The Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra
$\mathcal{W}_3^{(2)}$ is strict (canonical arity~$2$),
$\mathcal{W}_4^{(2)}$ has a genuine cubic Taylor coefficient, and
$\mathcal{W}_n^{(2)}$ has canonical arity~$n-1$ for all~$n \ge 3$.
The subregular family traces a staircase of increasing homotopy
complexity --- from strict, to cubic, to arbitrarily high arity ---
indexed by the rank.

\subsection{PBW--Slodowy collapse}
\label{subsec:pbw-slodowy-collapse}

\begin{definition}[Filtered-complete chiral algebra]
\label{def:w-filtered-complete-chiral}
\index{filtered-complete chiral algebra}
A chiral or vertex algebra~$A$ equipped with an exhaustive separated
increasing filtration
\[
F_0A \subset F_1A \subset F_2A \subset \cdots \subset A
\]
that is multiplicative and compatible with~$\partial$ is
\emph{filtered-complete}.  Its \emph{completed reduced bar complex}
$\widehat{\overline{B}}(A)$ is the completion of the usual reduced
bar complex with respect to the induced filtration by total
$F$-degree.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Completed Koszulity]
\label{def:w-completed-koszulity}
\index{completed Koszulity!definition}
A filtered-complete chiral algebra~$A$ is \emph{completed Koszul} if
the homology of $\widehat{\overline{B}}(A)$ is concentrated on the
diagonal with respect to bar grading and induced filtration grading,
equivalently if the completed cobar of this homology reconstructs $A$
up to filtered quasi-isomorphism.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[PBW--Slodowy collapse; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-pbw-slodowy-collapse}
\index{PBW--Slodowy collapse}
\index{spectral sequence!E1 collapse@$E_1$ collapse}
Let $A$ be a filtered chiral algebra such that:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the filtration is exhaustive, separated, and multiplicative;
\item every conformal-weight piece is finite-dimensional and the
filtration is bounded below on each weight;
\item there is an isomorphism of differential-commutative graded
algebras
\[
\operatorname{gr}_F A
\cong \operatorname{Sym}_\partial(V)
:= \operatorname{Sym}\!\Bigl(
   \bigoplus_{m \ge 0}\partial^m V\Bigr)
\]
for a finite-dimensional vector space~$V$.
\end{enumerate}
Then the completed bar spectral sequence of~$A$, filtered by total
$F$-degree, collapses at~$E_1$ and
\[
H_*\!\bigl(\widehat{\overline{B}}(A)\bigr)
\cong \widehat{\Lambda}_\partial(sV)
\]
as completed coalgebras.  In particular, $A$ is completed Koszul and
admits a canonical completed cobar model
\[
\widehat{\Omega}\,\widehat{\Lambda}_\partial(sV)
\xrightarrow{\;\simeq\;} A.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Filter $\overline{B}(A)$ by total $F$-degree.  Multiplicativity
identifies the $E_0$-page with the reduced bar complex of the
associated graded:
\[
E_0 \cong \overline{B}(\operatorname{gr}_F A)
= \overline{B}(\operatorname{Sym}_\partial(V)).
\]
The bar homology of the free differential polynomial algebra on~$V$
is the exterior coalgebra on the suspended derivative generators:
\[
H_*\!\bigl(\overline{B}(\operatorname{Sym}_\partial(V))\bigr)
\cong \Lambda_\partial(sV).
\]
Indeed, $\operatorname{Sym}_\partial(V)$ is a tensor product of
polynomial algebras on the generators $\partial^m v$, and the reduced
bar homology of a polynomial algebra is exterior on the suspension.

The $E_1$-page is concentrated on the diagonal, so every higher
differential vanishes for bidegree reasons.  Weightwise convergence
follows from the finite-dimensionality hypothesis.  The spectral
sequence collapses at $E_1$, and after completion one obtains the
stated coalgebra identification.  The canonical twisting cochain from
the bar homology to $A$ yields the completed cobar
reconstruction.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Principal $W$-algebras are completed Koszul;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:w-principal-completed-koszul}
\index{completed Koszulity!principal W-algebra@principal $\mathcal{W}$-algebra}
Let $\mathfrak{g}$ be simple and $f_{\mathrm{prin}}$ principal.  For
$k \neq -h^\vee$, the universal affine $W$-algebra
$\mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g}, f_{\mathrm{prin}})$ is completed
Koszul.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Arakawa's theorem on the Li filtration in the principal case, the
associated graded is the coordinate ring of the arc space of the
Kostant slice:
\[
\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{Li}}
  \mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g}, f_{\mathrm{prin}})
\cong \mathbb{C}[J\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{prin}}].
\]
The Kostant slice $\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{prin}}
= f_{\mathrm{prin}} + \mathfrak{g}^e$ is affine, hence
\[
\mathbb{C}[J\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{prin}}]
\cong \operatorname{Sym}_\partial\bigl((\mathfrak{g}^e)^*\bigr).
\]
Apply Theorem~\ref{thm:w-pbw-slodowy-collapse} with
$V = (\mathfrak{g}^e)^*$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Extension to arbitrary nilpotent data]
\label{rem:w-arbitrary-nilpotent-completed-koszul}
\index{completed Koszulity!arbitrary nilpotent}
The same argument applies to
$\mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g}, f)$ whenever
$\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{Li}} \mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g}, f)
\cong \mathbb{C}[J\mathcal{S}_f]$
with $\mathcal{S}_f = f + \mathfrak{g}^e$ affine.  Since every
Slodowy slice is affine, the completed-Koszul problem for general
affine $W$-algebras reduces to establishing the associated-graded
identification in each case.  In the subregular case, this
identification is known, so subregular $W$-algebras at generic level
are also completed Koszul.
\end{remark}

\subsection{A normal-form criterion for canonical arity}
\label{subsec:canonical-arity-detection}

Completed Koszulity is the global statement; the canonical arity of
the completed dual is the local refinement that measures exactly how
far from ``quadratic'' the dual structure reaches.

\begin{definition}[Canonical homotopy arity]
\label{def:w-canonical-homotopy-arity}
\index{canonical homotopy arity}
Fix an ordered strong generating set
$X_1, \dots, X_N$ for a filtered-complete chiral algebra~$A$.  The
reduced bar differential on the completed tensor coalgebra
$T^c(sV)$ decomposes into Taylor coefficients
\[
d = d_0 + d_1 + d_2 + d_3 + \cdots, \qquad
d_r \colon sV \to (sV)^{\otimes r}.
\]
The maximal nonzero Taylor arity is the \emph{canonical homotopy
arity} of $A$ in the given normal form.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Canonical arity detection;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-canonical-arity-detection}
\index{canonical arity detection}
Let $A$ be presented in a fixed normal form by strong generators
$X_1, \dots, X_N$.  If every singular OPE coefficient is a normally
ordered differential polynomial of generator degree at most~$d$, then
\[
d_r = 0 \qquad (r > d).
\]
If, moreover, some singular coefficient contains a
generator-degree-$d$ term surviving in the chosen normal form, then
$d_d \neq 0$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Taylor coefficient $d_r$ is dual to the generator-degree-$r$
part of the singular OPE normal form.  If no OPE coefficient contains
terms of generator degree $> d$, then no Taylor coefficient of arity
$> d$ can appear.  Conversely, a nonzero degree-$d$ term contributes
a nonzero arity-$d$ Taylor coefficient under dualization.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra: strictness}
\label{subsec:bershadsky-polyakov-strict}

\begin{theorem}[Bershadsky--Polyakov is strict;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-bp-strict}
\index{Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra!strictness}
For $k \neq -3$, the canonical normalized completed dual of the
Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra $\mathcal{W}_3^{(2)}(k)$ has
\[
d_r = 0 \qquad (r \ge 3).
\]
Its canonical homotopy arity is~$2$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Feigin--Semikhatov OPEs of $\mathcal{W}_3^{(2)}$ are
\begin{align*}
E(z)F(w)
&= \frac{(k+1)(2k+3)}{(z-w)^3}
 + \frac{3(k+1)H(w)}{(z-w)^2}
 + \frac{3{:}HH{:}(w) - (k+3)T(w)
         + \tfrac{3}{2}(k+1)\partial H(w)}{z-w},
\\[4pt]
H(z)H(w)
&\sim \frac{2k+3}{3(z-w)^2}, \qquad
H(z)E(w) \sim \frac{E(w)}{z-w}, \qquad
H(z)F(w) \sim -\frac{F(w)}{z-w}.
\end{align*}
Every singular coefficient has generator degree at most~$2$: the
only nonlinear term is the quadratic monomial ${:}HH{:}$ in the
simple pole of $E(z)F(w)$.  Apply
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-canonical-arity-detection} with $d = 2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Strictness as completed quadratic duality]
\label{rem:w-bp-strictness-meaning}
Strictness means that the completed dual of the
Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra is a genuine dg algebra (a curved
$A_\infty$-algebra with $d_r = 0$ for $r \ge 3$), not merely a
curved $A_\infty$-algebra with higher operations.  The bar-cobar
inversion theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:w-koszul-precise}) therefore
operates in its simplest form.  This is in sharp contrast to the
principal $\mathcal{W}_3$ algebra, which is semistrict but not
strict: the $\{W_\lambda W\}$ bracket has generator-degree~$2$ in
the generators, producing a nonzero ternary Taylor coefficient.  The
first subregular algebra in the hierarchy is \emph{simpler} than the
principal one.
\end{remark}

\subsection{$\mathcal{W}_4^{(2)}$ and the first cubic obstruction}
\label{subsec:w4-subregular-cubic}

\begin{theorem}[$\mathcal{W}_4^{(2)}$ has canonical arity~$3$;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-w4-cubic}
\index{W-algebra@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra!W4 subregular@$\mathcal{W}_4^{(2)}$ cubic}
For every $k$ with $(k+2)(11k+32) \neq 0$, the canonical normalized
completed dual of $\mathcal{W}_4^{(2)}(k)$ has $d_3 \neq 0$.  Its
canonical homotopy arity is at least~$3$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Feigin--Semikhatov's explicit formula for the $E$--$F$ OPE of
$\mathcal{W}_4^{(2)}$ contains in the simple pole the cubic
Heisenberg term
\[
-\frac{8(k+2)(11k+32)}{3(3k+8)^2}\,H^3(w),
\]
which is nonzero under the stated genericity condition.  This is a
generator-degree-$3$ monomial in the Feigin--Semikhatov normal form.
Apply Theorem~\ref{thm:w-canonical-arity-detection} with $d = 3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Essential nature of the cubic term]
\label{rem:w-w4-cubic-essential}
The neutral weight-$3$ generator $W$ of $\mathcal{W}_4^{(2)}$ is
characterized by being Virasoro primary and regular with respect
to~$H$.  Any redefinition preserving this normalization can shift
linear and derivative contributions but cannot eliminate the pure
$H^3$ term without leaving the $H$-regular gauge.  Thus the cubic
obstruction is not a normal-form artifact; it is an intrinsic
homotopical feature of the subregular $\mathfrak{sl}_4$ algebra.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The exact coefficient packet via Bell recursion}
\label{subsec:exact-bell-recursion}

The Feigin--Semikhatov realization provides the exact singular OPE
coefficients for the entire subregular family through a single
recursive formula.

\begin{definition}[Recursive coefficient operators]
\label{def:w-recursive-coefficient-operators}
\index{recursive coefficient operators!subregular}
For fixed~$n$, set $K_n := k + n - 1$ and
$u_j := Q + A_1 + \cdots + A_j$ for $0 \le j \le n-1$, with
$u_0 = Q$.  Define differential polynomials
$\mathcal{C}_{j,m} = \mathcal{C}_{j,m}^{(n,k)}$ recursively by
\[
\mathcal{C}_{0,0} = 1, \qquad
\mathcal{C}_{j,m} = 0 \;\text{ if } m < 0 \text{ or } m > j,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal{C}_{j+1,m}
= \bigl(K_n(j-m) - 1\bigr)\,\mathcal{C}_{j,m}
+ \bigl(K_n\partial + u_j\bigr)\mathcal{C}_{j,m-1}
\qquad (0 \le m \le j+1).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Full raw coefficient packet;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-full-raw-coefficient-packet}
\index{OPE coefficient packet!subregular}
In the maximally asymmetric realization of
$\mathcal{W}_n^{(2)}(k)$, let $B_a(Y, \partial Y, \dots)$ denote
the Bell polynomials of the exponential factor (defined by
$\exp(\sum_{r \ge 0} t^{r+1}\partial^r Y/(r+1)!)
= \sum_{a \ge 0} t^a B_a/a!$).  Setting $t = z - w$, one has
\[
E_n(z)F_n(w)
= \sum_{r=0}^{n-1} \frac{U_{n,r}^{\mathrm{raw}}(w)}{t^{n-r}}
  + O(t^0),
\]
where the singular coefficients are
\[
U_{n,r}^{\mathrm{raw}}
= -\sum_{a=0}^{r} \frac{1}{a!}\,
  B_a(Y, \partial Y, \dots, \partial^{a-1}Y)\,
  \mathcal{C}_{n,r-a}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Feigin--Semikhatov generator is
\[
F_n(w) = -\bigl((K_n\partial + u_{n-1})
  \circ \cdots \circ (K_n\partial + u_0)\bigr) e^{-\Xi}(w).
\]
Moving $e^{\Xi}(z)$ past the ordered product by Wick expansion
replaces each factor $K_n\partial_w + u_j(w)$ by the ordered
operator $K_n\partial_w + u_j(w) - t^{-1}$ acting to the right.
Define $R_j(t)$ as the result of applying the first $j$ modified
factors to~$1$, and expand
$R_j(t) = \sum_m \mathcal{C}_{j,m}\,t^{-(j-m)}$.  The recursion
of Definition~\ref{def:w-recursive-coefficient-operators} follows
from applying one additional factor and using
$\partial_w(t^{-p}) = p\,t^{-(p+1)}$.  Multiplying the expansion of
$R_n(t)$ by the Bell polynomial expansion of
$e^{\Xi(z) - \Xi(w)}$ and collecting coefficients gives the
displayed formula.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The subregular Appell formula}
\label{subsec:subregular-appell}

The highest generator-degree content of the coefficient packet is
isolated by a derivative-killing symbol map
$\sigma \colon \mathbb{C}[Q, A_i, Y, \partial Q, \dots]
\to \mathbb{C}[q, a_i, y]$
that kills all derivatives and sends $Q \mapsto q$, $A_i \mapsto a_i$,
$Y \mapsto y$.  In these coordinates
$u_j = q + a_1 + \cdots + a_j$, and the symbol of the Miura product
is $\sigma(P_n^{(k)}) = \prod_{j=0}^{n-1} u_j$.

Introduce the center-of-mass variable
$h_n := \frac{1}{n}\sum_{j=0}^{n-1} u_j$ and the centered variables
$v_j := u_j - h_n$ with $\sum_j v_j = 0$.  Let $e_r(v)$ denote the
$r$-th elementary symmetric polynomial in $v_0, \dots, v_{n-1}$.

\begin{theorem}[Subregular Appell formula; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-subregular-appell}
\index{Appell formula!subregular}
For $2 \le r \le n-1$, the leading symbol of the weight-$r$ raw
coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:w-subregular-appell}
C_{n,r}(h_n, v)
= \frac{1}{(n-r)!}\,\partial_q^{\,n-r}
  \Bigl(\prod_{j=0}^{n-1} u_j\Bigr)
= \sum_{t=0}^{r} \binom{n-r+t}{t}\,e_{r-t}(v)\,h_n^t.
\end{equation}
In particular, $\partial_{h_n} C_{n,r} = (n-r+1)\,C_{n,r-1}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since $\prod_j u_j = \prod_j (h_n + v_j)$ and the $v_j$ are
independent of~$q$ while $\partial_q h_n = 1$, we have
$\partial_q^{\,n-r}/(n-r)!
= \partial_{h_n}^{\,n-r}/(n-r)!$.  Expand the product in elementary
symmetric functions:
$\prod_j (h_n + v_j) = \sum_{s=0}^n e_{n-s}(v)\,h_n^s$.
Differentiating termwise and writing $s = n - r + t$ gives
$\binom{n-r+t}{t}\,h_n^t$ for each summand.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Normalized symbols]
\label{rem:w-normalized-symbols}
The variable $h_n$ is the Heisenberg direction, while the
translation-invariant part $e_r(v)$ is the normalized symbol of the
new neutral generator at weight~$r$.  The Appell formula separates
the Heisenberg tower from the $H$-orthogonal generator content at
the symbolic level.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Unbounded canonical arity in the subregular line}
\label{subsec:unbounded-arity}

\begin{theorem}[Unbounded canonical arity; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-unbounded-canonical-arity}
\index{canonical homotopy arity!unbounded}
For generic level $k$ and every $n \ge 3$, the canonical normalized
completed dual of $\mathcal{W}_n^{(2)}(k)$ has nonzero Taylor
coefficients in all arities $2 \le r \le n-1$.  The canonical
homotopy arity of the subregular family is unbounded as
$n \to \infty$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For $n = 3$, Theorem~\ref{thm:w-bp-strict} gives canonical arity~$2$.
For $n = 4$, Theorem~\ref{thm:w-w4-cubic} gives $d_3 \neq 0$.  For
general~$n$, the Appell formula
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-subregular-appell}) shows that the weight-$r$ raw
coefficient has symbolic expansion
\[
C_{n,r}(h_n, v) = e_r(v) + \binom{n-r+1}{1}\,e_{r-1}(v)\,h_n
+ \cdots + \binom{n}{r}\,h_n^r.
\]
The term $\binom{n}{r}\,h_n^r$ is nonzero for every
$2 \le r \le n-1$, so the weight-$r$ singular coefficient contains a
generator-degree-$r$ contribution in the centered normal form.  Apply
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-canonical-arity-detection}: the canonical
completed dual has nonzero Taylor coefficient~$d_r$ for each
$r \le n-1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[The subregular arity staircase;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:w-subregular-arity-staircase}
\index{arity staircase!subregular}
The subregular family in type $A$ exhibits the following canonical
arity staircase:
\[
\begin{array}{c|ccccc}
n & 3 & 4 & 5 & 6 & \cdots \\
\hline
\text{canonical arity} & 2 & 3 & 4 & 5 & \cdots
\end{array}
\]
Equivalently, $\mathcal{W}_n^{(2)}$ at generic level has canonical
homotopy arity exactly $n - 1$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
That the canonical arity is $\ge n-1$ follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-unbounded-canonical-arity}.  The upper bound
follows because the $E_n$--$F_n$ OPE has $n$ singular
poles (so the maximal generator degree in the raw coefficients is
at most $n-1$) and from
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-canonical-arity-detection}.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[Minimal arity survives generically;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:w-minimal-arity-subregular}
\index{minimal arity conjecture!subregular}
For generic~$k$, the minimal transferred completed dual of
$\mathcal{W}_n^{(2)}(k)$ has maximal nonzero arity exactly $n-1$.
Equivalently, the canonical arities detected in
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-unbounded-canonical-arity} survive minimal-model
transfer.
\end{conjecture}

\subsection{The classification package}
\label{subsec:subregular-classification}

The completed Koszulity theorem and the arity staircase together
yield a clean structural classification of the subregular family.

\begin{theorem}[Subregular classification; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w-subregular-classification}
\index{W-algebra@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra!subregular classification}
For the subregular family $\mathcal{W}_n^{(2)}$ in type~$A$ at
generic level:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Each $\mathcal{W}_n^{(2)}$ is completed Koszul
(Corollary~\ref{cor:w-principal-completed-koszul} and
Remark~\ref{rem:w-arbitrary-nilpotent-completed-koszul}).

\item The canonical homotopy arity is exactly $n-1$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:w-subregular-arity-staircase}).

\item $\mathcal{W}_3^{(2)}$ (Bershadsky--Polyakov) is the unique
strict member (Theorem~\ref{thm:w-bp-strict}).

\item $\mathcal{W}_4^{(2)}$ is the first member with a genuine
cubic Taylor coefficient
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-w4-cubic}).

\item The full singular OPE packet is determined recursively by the
Bell formula of Theorem~\ref{thm:w-full-raw-coefficient-packet}, and
the highest-arity content is governed by the Appell formula of
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-subregular-appell}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Each statement has been proved in the indicated theorem or corollary.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Comparison with the principal family]
\label{rem:w-subregular-vs-principal}
\index{W-algebra@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra!principal vs.\ subregular}
The principal $\mathcal{W}_N$ family is conjecturally $N$-strict
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:w-finite-arity-WN}), with arity growing
linearly in the rank --- but the principal algebras are obtained from
quadratic DS reduction of $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}$, and their
nonlinearity is generated entirely by the $\{W_\lambda W\}$ brackets
through the Sugawara-type composites.  The subregular family has a
different origin: it arises from the Feigin--Semikhatov
free-field realization, and the growing arity is encoded in the
combinatorial explosion of the ordered Miura product
$\prod_{j=0}^{n-1} u_j$.  Thus the principal and subregular families
represent two qualitatively different mechanisms for generating
homotopy complexity: compositional nonlinearity (principal) versus
combinatorial depth of the screening resolution (subregular).  The
former is conjecturally bounded by the number of generators; the
latter grows with the rank regardless of the generator count.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Geometric meaning]
\label{rem:w-subregular-geometric-meaning}
The PBW filtration is controlled by Slodowy slices and their
arc spaces.  The homotopy arity is controlled by the failure of the
quantized slice to remain quadratic after one chooses a strong
generating set and performs chiral normal ordering.  In the
Bershadsky--Polyakov case ($n = 3$), the Slodowy slice is
$\mathfrak{sl}_3^{e_{\mathrm{subreg}}}$, which is two-dimensional,
and the normal ordering produces only quadratic corrections.  For
$n \ge 4$, the slice dimension grows and the screening-mediated
normal-ordering corrections introduce genuinely new cubic, quartic,
$\dots$, $(n-1)$-ary terms.  The subregular family thus traces
the transition from classical to homotopical Koszul duality,
parameterized by the simplest geometric invariant: the dimension of
the Slodowy slice.
\end{remark}
